Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse of what we have said in the divisions of the treatments, and it does not help, then there are three kinds of cauteries that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which some manner is that you make III cauteries, or IIII, lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not hasten your hand to the whole cautery, and let the patient be lying on his back; and another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has II nerves, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is at the mouse, or the cuts of the patient come from the left, and let the elevation which you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries be according to the width of the body. 
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After he puts the two nerves on fire until the kernels are pierced from the other side, and then removes the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you see it, then cauterize with the whole cautery to three nerves. 
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten rot for a long time, and this is worth moving than the other cures before said. 
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterizing is not good for dropsy, except for the manner called "asclytes". 
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make IIII cauteries around the head, and I on the stomach, and one on the liver, and I on the spleen, and II behind the back on the spine, and I in the middle of the breast; and let the cauteries be near the heart.  
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After let the cautery uncovered for to fight putrefaction long time, and do not leave the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing would hasten, and will be together the two intentions with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the clavicle that we have before shows; and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is set forth above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in those who are hydrophic, and are full of a we citrine, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning. 
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too much by the font, so tightly close the outer edge of the awl, and let the cautery be according to this form. 
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After do on .ij. legs .ij. cauteries in each leg at the tip of the curette; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open lengthwise without curing, that they may rise in them; after the cure of the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When belly solution comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which is in the stomach and in the intestine is weakened, and cannot be cured by means of cures; and you see the patient suffering much and of great virtue, then do one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, to the circulating cautery; and four cauteries around the navel subtle, at each cautery a subtle cleaver, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are at the base, or one or more, and they are old and are of large cold and moist humors corrupted, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, if you do cauteries: III on the spine of the back, which is all outside almecate poc and poc by triangulating, and I cautery below the mound II does; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then one does I great cautery on the stomach, as it is said before, and I other on the liver, and I other on the mice to all the cautery clavicle; and leave the cautery open for a long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cure the place until it is healed. 
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the "thelul," sharpen the cautery which seems like i. razor, and then put it all ablaze on that "thelul"  cut; and let it there as long as the cauteries reach the birth of the vein, so that the blood does not clot; do this once or twice, and if there is much "thelul," cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of ointments beneficial until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the "alchatim," it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will relate in its place, such a malady comes that it can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When to any comes fistula, and is filled and full of rottenness and corrupt moisture, then it does well to quickly provide a fine tent, and guard that you know at all the tent how much it has in circumference. 
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After the cautery which seems to be the razor, and put it in the fistula according to the quantity that it tested was entered, and restart the cautery until the flesh and corrupt are burned, once, or II or III, according to the quantity of the need; and guard against hurting the nerves which are inside, and the large veins. 
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, then guard these places, and do not make those fuers than in the fleshy place, and think that it is not pierced; after cure the place until it is healed, and if the places are saielez, and the matters are removed long time, then know that the place is healed entirely; and if the matters are not removed, know that the place is false, and corrupted the bone at the root; and so as one of these that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	of the kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes as rains, and of great windiness, and does not take much of a woman, then it is necessary that you make cautery on the loins on one side and the other with the cautery clavicle that we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in line, and they will do more help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and feeble from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then I make cautery in the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery as long as our finger; and I make one cautery outside the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauteries be clavicle according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow for those to conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are late; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore it is necessary that one make three cauteries around the bud, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back; and let the cauteries be clavil, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the bone of the hip, and for this cause it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together; and it is found the level of the viscus department, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the bone of the hip with one cautery resembling a circle, and sign before the place around the bone as it turns, so that the bone be inside the circle; and let the cautery be such as the one with which the stomach was cauterized.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, make .iij. cauteries of the olive large, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; and cure it until it is sound.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the socket of the hip, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of those things that we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say together medicines burning, and cautery of fire. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is done in many ways, one of which is as follows: that you cauterize on the bone of the hip III triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them good depth and large, and there be between each cautery a space the size of a digit, and let the cauteries be olive; sometimes one makes cautery in the middle on the top of the hip, for which reason there are IIII according to this form:  
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see it, cauterize it with the cautery of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do in such a manner that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the heart are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner one does in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg. 
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and leg, make two cauteries there where the patient says the pain holds him, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers wide, on the left side a little; and whether the cautery is made with a curette or burnt with the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the two fingers of the foot or near it, then cauterize it where he feels the pain three fingers or four at the cautery called "finger".  
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, then one does more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee toward the thigh, then one makes a cautery with the pointed or circular cautery; and well guard in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery there so much that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and that you do no more nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have made cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left them until the leg was all swollen, and the foot as well, and it was pierced and corrupted the whole foot. 
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a belly ache of which he had death. 
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and the other, according to this manner.  
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sage said in the cautery of the hip, for this is the manner, make such iron and be at the chief as big as a nail of finger, or a little less, and be between entanglements and be from one entanglement to the other by spacing the quantity of a node of fist; and be the entanglements on two parts, and be also like nuts, and there is in the hip of iron well made; and this is the form:  
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is all red and feel its heat, and then put it on the bone of the diseased hip, and be turned on the healthy side; and cauterize once one cautery return and leave it three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound uncovered for a long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its regard, and we see few who use it; and nonetheless these are good cauteries, which can bear it, and where it is needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of medicine burning are so that you make the instrument in a  rectangle as it descends on the edge of the door, and be of iron or steel to one side long, and in the height have II noses, and have between each the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and be open outward and upward, and join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After place the bolster of the hip upon the patient lying on his healthy side, and press your hand strongly upon the bolster of the hip; after put between the two circles of the hot awl which is heated in the fire one point, and let him for an hour of the time, and suffer the patient the heat and the burn of it. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is found moderation also with fire; and when the moderation is passed, raise your hand with the instrument and lift the hip away gently, and leave thus III days, and put on butter until that which is black from the scald is removed; and leave it III days that rot may extract itself; and this would be the last aid after the cure of wounds as long as it is sound. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that holds it down according to what you have done in the hip augmentation; and this is the manner of the hot awl, and I have written it or treated it in the rectification of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot. 
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small hole in the fire, so that the point of a razor can enter; and put one pot on top of the other well closed, and put alkali and salt and honey on top, as long as there is the right amount of powder on top until you have taken it well with your hand; and let it remain like this until the honey goes down and drips or closes, then take all that honey and put it on the salt and alkali like before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then if it will be much heat and is administered in the work of medicine and cauteries of other members Because she does some work like fire, and has other medicines with which one cauterizes well the hip as well as honey tessie and almond nut and chalk with soap, all these things mixed together. 
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Galicians tell us a cure of a man who was cured of hip pain and sciatica, and he praised it very much, and said that no other cure was made, and he was healed in a single time when this cure was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches afterwards.   
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And say in such a manner that you take of the green litharge fresh and dry, and grind it well with a little bit of grease, and put on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain holds, and the groin; and leave it III hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning. 
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter into the bath until the body is a little aroused, and let him enter into bed, and the pain will go away all and will be healed. 
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cautery of such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of the body. 
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with a fire of goat, it helps much; and it must be done the cautery in such manner. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lamb's wool and soak it with old oil, and put it on the fossa which is between the thumb and foot and the other one called fossa. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After take fibers of dry goat, and put it in fire until it is charcoal, and put it on the wool, and let it stay until it is extinguished; and redo as much, and do not cease to do so until you think by sense that it comes up to the hip, and that the pain is ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat". 
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or from percussion or by excessive evacuation, or from similar appearances of cold matter spread, none of these appearances are worth cautery except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be void of fetid pills or other similar things, that on him be made upon his back, where the pain holds, three lines signed with inche, and in each line .v. cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make .iij. cauteries or .iiij. at the clavile cautery mean according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight belly when they cry, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and want to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this kind according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery sear each part of the spine equally. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointed II lines or III, and let the points be near each other.  
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After cure the place as long as it is sound according to what we have said, and ward that you do not administer cautery in a nerve-spasm which is in spasm. 
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is from moisture that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, that which they call "gout" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the fire cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you grasp on the face of the foot, then make the cautery to all the cautery as one claims “point”. 
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then you do cautery on each knee III cauteries or IIII of each part, at all the olive cautery; and if you need more, make more, but don't hold your hand forcefully except as long as the tip of the heart is burned. 
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and to the back, administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter. 
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, so make poins around the wrist II lines; and if there remains no pain to the two, so make poins on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or to the shoulders, so cauterize each part, and make good governance to the patient and careful medicines.  
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes in the arms, and the tendons descend to the elbows, it is newly, so when you see him cured, that he does not move it on that day; and that he uses things that hold up his belly, so that the fibers descend from his belly; after that make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm as long as the tendons are repaired, and straighten them towards your thumbs, and sign of a circle under the rupture on the bone of the shoulder, and with a whole sign that is similar to half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of this which is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and he feels them 
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so that they do not return backward; and work well the legs of the patient, and put under him the cushion and the sergeant on the thighs, and the other above the hip which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and keep it straight and as far as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, begin again once more until you come to the bone; and be careful that the bone does not jump out when you make the cautery; so that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die, or other damage. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And knows that when you do not come close to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. 
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of them, and of great people also as large according to their measure; after III days cure their place with butter until the burn is removed; after the cure of other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie XL days on his back until the wound is well joined; and it is necessary that its dressings be loosened lengthways so that the boil does not stick out when he tries to go into rooms. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, have a good bandage made for him, and keep it on for another 40 days; and have good rest, that he work little and guard against too much drinking and eating, and too much high braising; and when he does this teaching so is healed entirely. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall say after this the treatment of tailoring in its chapter. 
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then make the cautery of cautery according to its quantity, and be it at the third part of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said one must cauterize with the cautery at III angles according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first sign the place of the joint and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another below, and hold your hand over all the fire cautery clavicle. 
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and quicker. 
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of ancient pain in no limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or striking, and this pain lasts a long time, and the care of medicine does not work, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "poins," and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain. 
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for such custom is that it must be burned to the member that is nearest, therefore it behoves you to make the cauteries as long as the patient is unhealed. 
de meselerie	of surgery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The wounds are aided at times by cautery with great help, and even the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. 
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Since you can see it being cauterized, take care that the patient is at the beginning, and if she has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not send or remain, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the patient, then you make V cauteries on the head: I am putting the chief to nine, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and II on the II horns, and I behind on the haiterel; and leave as long as your hand that the cauteries come to the bone, and as long as the peels exit out so that the vapors of the gross humors can issue from it; and cauterize on the mice according to what it is in front.  
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mesentery is spread everywhere; and it manifests clearly, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and one cautery on its navel, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one great one on the crupie and one other under, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the arms, and two on the tendons of the hip, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and guard against the nerves that are on the last calf, that you do not burn them; and sometimes it is done cauterizing on the bone of the arm, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when more is done with cautery, it does more aid, and moves it profit; and know that the patient feels no pain from cautery as the healthy feel it, because the body is already wholly corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in methods of irons. 
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After curing the place with flour of rice mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healed. 
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any limb and is treated by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery be a point entering into the thickness of the skin; then cure with dressings until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at times one makes cautery and to the hand and to the foot and to the back, at the exit of the nerve that numbs the limb, and thus so is removed the swelling; and all the way does not intervene any one if he is not knowledgeable about the members and about the exits of the nerves moving the body.  
de albaras	from girdles
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the malady that is called "albaras" is present, and the means of medicine avail nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery one prick through, according to the quantity of the thickness of the flesh, until the blemish is removed, and its color changed; then cure with flour of vicees and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alondre, of each one part; and mix all together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of sores by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre comes at the beginning, and you see it arrested, then cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the circumference of the sore. 
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nonetheless the wise men say that one should make a cautery in the middle of the sore; and nonetheless this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted it to happen any time; and more right thing is that it be cauterized around, at the cautery which is called "circulus", as we have said in many cauteries.  
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some one has an illness that is called «adubelati», and it is slow to die or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the blood of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the heat; and you see it hasten to die: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries in pricking; after that leave it so. 
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die. 
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce with all the cautery, so heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of the illness that is called «adubelati» until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning in such a manner that the course of the rot is raised. 
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until it is perfectly healed. 
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	A different kind of illness there is called “corroding,” and it is nothing other than a consumption of the limb, because it consumes the limbs like dry ropes.  
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can endure fire cautery, then sharpen the cautery hooks very small and large, according to what is fitting for the place where the malady is; after that cauterize from all sides until you eradicate all corruption, and nothing of it remains, that all that is corrupted be removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for III days, and put on the cauterized places bruised with oil until the scars from the fire are removed, and all the corruption. 
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of ingrowing flesh. 
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after III days that the carbuncle is not healing, it's good; and if it isn't, begin the cautery again on those which are remaining corrupt. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this malady is sometimes cured with hot medicine in place of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already said the cure for hot medicine in the division: take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the  sprouts which come to the foot
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that by fire a disease is born in the feet which is called "closed" according to our understanding, and is a great thing that spoils the foot.  
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this illness is according to II manners. 
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and cautery of hot water. 
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cauterizing with fire is that you heat the iron cautery as a goose feather, and it is made of good iron to the measure that it can bend the nail from all sides, and that it has subtle edges; after putting the whole hot on the nail, and turning your hand around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and let it this way for III days until it begins to rot; then I make a poultice of wild mallows crushed with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nails will fall out and be uprooted from their roots.   
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place with ointment hindering flesh until it is sound. 
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happen in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you bring them cautery of hot water; and it is in such manner: take a chain of iron or of steel, or a feather of vulture, and put upon the nail and the nail, that is to say porrelz warts; and put the chain on so that it wraps all around, then put a drop of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the chain comes to the root of the nail, and may find the hot water path deep to the root; and let the patient suffer a bit the burning of the hot water an hour; then let him go as it is, and it will be eradicated all its roots. 
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you have searched all those that are in the body, then treat the ailments that cause flesh. 
li cure dou trembler	the cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or fever quartan or other, so it befits that you make to him .iv. cauteries or .iii. on the spine of the back, .i. cautery between each spine; and .i. cautery or weight, and .i. on the stomach at the olive cautery; so will leave the trembling, and hastens the saint health from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	of festering pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	At no time appear by fire the body bathed, or pimples coming from large rotten matters.  
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary in the first place when they appear that one does cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle stick, so that the point be grasped by the fire, or from root of long aristolochia, or to the lenticular cautery. 
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes the cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from within forward, but are disrupted the superfluities from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great spurts of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nonetheless when this happens to anyone, quickly put your finger on the wound of the vein, and restrain it very tightly until the bleeding is appeased under your finger, and no drop comes out anymore; then put to fire the olive cauteries more small and large as much as they are all red; then take one, or a great one or a small one according to the wound and its place where the artery is routed, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it leaps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily one other of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do these one after the other until the vein is stretched; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is beside it, and that another malice does not come upon the patient; and know that when a vein departs from the artery, one cannot well stretch it, even when the artery is great, unless by one of the four manners that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding of thread, or by medicines put upon it which have power to stretch veins; and be bound and restrained well.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring a stretching of ligaments tightly by straps or by putting things burning on it, or other similar things, if it does not profit to this?
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no medicine present, then he should put his right index finger upon the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well until it is stretched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but often wet with cold water so that it be very cold until the vein is congealed and thickened and stretched; and make from then on those things which he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of cures of the tail
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the maladies in which it is necessary cautery of fire, or ardent medicine, and the incisions and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have put that chapter from the head jus to the foot, and I will go in this chapter by that same way for those who find it more easily what they want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, it is necessary, dear pupil, that you learn that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in the first of cauteries, and for that reason it is necessary more great caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. 
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to cures.  
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from such who have endured so much with their illness that they die easily because of the forcefulness that they find in their illness, and of the greatness of their malice; and of these one must have fear. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are some who give you their meaning, and say: “wait, I am healed”; and the patient is deceitful. 
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not appropriate that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your desire, and do not work foolishly but wisely of those whom you are certain, and whom you can have taken and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the cures of your patients so that health may be converted; and these will help you to acquire a good reputation, and glory, and long memory. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, May our Lords give you good understanding and rightness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter to you in devising by chapters, according to those that it is before or chapter of cauteries, which I have devised from the chief to foot, for those that you find more easily those that you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The chief full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes many times to children at birth, and when the midwife strains too hard the head of the child; and sometimes it comes from a reason unknown
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness outside of children, and to all those that I have seen it has hastened death; and for that reason it seems to me that it is better for me to leave the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose shoulder was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until he could not support it; and he thought so much because of the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled under the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and the work is like this if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you split in the middle of the head a wide fissure; and be also long as two fingers, as much as the moisture flows; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more thick, and the abscess is larger, do two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see the commissures of the shoulder open on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand inward, and this does not return to you: then it behooves you to split in the middle of the head three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision draw out the moisture all outside. 
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After restraining the incisions of cloth and powders, and put wine and oil on it, and leave like this until the fifth day; then untie it, and cure the wound with tents and ointments, and leave to restrain the main bandage, and then feed the patient dry meat from moisture as long as the limb is fortified and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where opens the greatness of the abscess, and its assembly of water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut where the abscess opens, and its filling of water, and  cut it according to what you have power; and guard that you do not cut the artery; and vein blood flows, so that the patient dies from the decrease of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of summary
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a sickness that is called “catarrh” at the eyes or at the chest, and the patient is old, and the cure of medicine does not profit, then the last cure is the cautery with those one covers the 2 arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It therefore behooves you, when you see them covered, that the patient make his head backward; after he rubs their place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then strain the patient's neck to all the cloth; then look where the vein sits, and the veins of one and the other are behind the ears, and so they are put back; then sign the veins with an incision, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula from the II part, until the tail comes to the bone, and that be by the wide of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, plunge the spatula under the artery and cover it above, cutting also as 2 fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood jumps out continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at feeling, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space of III points, then sign of the enche and make until the bone; and what it is necessary to put out blood is VI c/, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point of the syphac, so cover that pus does not come, then restrain the wound and tie, and the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
de emigrainne	Of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When a chronic migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to the moistures of tears and the heats in the temples and the old soreness and similar things, and it is medicated by ways of medicine and all that does not help him, then restrain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient makes rear the hairs of his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is poorly returned outwards than in some men who are too cold; and if it is returned, it strains the neck of the patient with some cloths, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and raises the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it above the pinches, and depart well from the webs that are under each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it to the tip of the awl, then cut from that part according to the quantity of the two parts. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not jump out all over without pain. 
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from the six to three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two leagues of a strong double silk thread, so that rotting does not come before the soldering of the wound, and there comes bleeding; then cut the superfluity which is between the two liens in the same hour, and then, if you see fit, you cauterize it with a cuticular cautery until the bones are reached as long as the chias are cut; and this is the middle work, if the patient has no fever and he is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is an aid to finish the moistures: for this reason it is of greater help to moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fill their place with old cotton and put on them tents well made; and when they are undone, let there be care with dry medicines which make flesh grow, and with tents, until it is healed; and if without a stop of the artery as much as you work on it, then hasten to cover by cautery, or you employ the place of vitriol and restrain it to your hand that the bleeding cease; and if you lack these present things, put on the place your cloth until the bleeding is congealed, and raise the place of cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be restrained as it should be; and what is better and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery trenchant by .ij. parts, but let the trenches be well spaced to keep longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thick, it holds less its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have between the two knives one and a half inches wide, and then when you have marked with the two points, and you put the red hot iron above as long as it comes up to the bone, and cut the vein in two points; and be distanced between the two shoulders because it is not joined together by this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are descending through the veins that are on the test of the head of fury, and it does not benefit any medicine if it is done, and you see the face of the patient twisting, and feels or front walking as if from shivering; and where the oil is wet and so much that the hair of the papers falls out, and the papers are chapped, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then there is need for this cure.
