Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in ancient times "a contused cure," and you do to the patient who has this disease the hairs that he have on his forehead, then you make III incisions on his forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one incision be as II should all remove the forehead down below until the nape, and the others II as II ribs above the cheekbones, and keep your incision from the arteries that are at II ribs above the cheekbones; and move your hand away from the continuation of the II jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of III does across the joins; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much of cloth for wiping the blood, then put the sharp spatula of II parts as here is the form: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is below the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the skin which is between the two incisions to all the fat that is on the bone, then make another from the middle incision until the other second, and then extract far this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put it in the first fissure the instrument which is called "cultellaire," and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the rib cutting toward the flesh near the heart, and the rib side towards the bone, and the blade until it comes to the middle fissure.  
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as the eyes as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches what opens to the heart, and then another part make in the middle fissure until the other end; and then extract blood equally, and press their place for the blood taken; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put on top cloths moistened in wine and oil and aisil, and keep that abscesses do not come; and on the third day untie the thread, and there administer a great poultice of water thyme, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures used for treating wounds, as long as it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any come catarrh acute accustomed, and you see the eyes closed and small, and weakening of sight, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where chief in perform a sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh do not come from many veins, and the mother cure that is, this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to rear his forehead, then make a wide cut in the middle of the forehead, and another one across its width. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begins from the cut of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the cut and put old cotton there, and linen bandages; then tie above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow, then cure it with drying things that make cartilage grow.  
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster from them; and administer it in these wounds to prevent cartilage growth entirely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the Stoppings of Ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which falls into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone of mine or similar thing as iron; or seed, as lentils, beans, peas; or flowing thing as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear, stone or any other manner of thing that does not fit in the ear, nor grows in the ear, then put the ear to the sun.  
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if there distills any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with condiment, and plug his nostrils when the sneezes come, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and hold the ear upward. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often comes strength by this cure; and if it does not come strength, to him administer the extraction with subtle pincers, for this is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the tweezers, it is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine single-edged needle; and if it does not come out by this, make a bird's beak of iron and thrust the head of the beak or hole into the ear very forcibly, and stop what is around the beak with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the beak; then try to force it out, because many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take glue of what birds use for their nests, and put it on any instrument which is pointed for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and try to force it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not follow all these things that we have said, then you haste to split the ear so that an abscess may come, and spasm; and the manner of splitting is that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and making a small split at the root of the ear in the fat or where it depends; and let the split be like a crescent moon, as far as you come to the bone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it carefully with your mouth; and care for it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue, then administer one spatula thin according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the ear is moist because of moisture from the ear, until you have made many parts of it; then extract with subtle pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	When water falls into the ear, it is appropriate for the patient to use a first-aid of condiments, and widen the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same ear where the water is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it leaps for this (reason), it is good.  
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it does not work, take many stones according to the length of your finger, light and thin, and heat them a little in the fire; and put it in the patient’s one ear opening, and pull on it from his feet on the other side, and place another stone on top of the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this of stone to stone until the water is all gone, and so will she come out completely; and if you see it, take a sprig, and put one end into the ear, and the other end hold on fire until the most tender part of the twig is burned; then make another piece of twigs as long as the water is all gone, as we have said in the stone. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, as a flea and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body which one can feel, then administer the extraction of pincers; and this is the thing more light to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not profit, then it behooves that you look at the ear in the sun: if there appears any worms, then treat them with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, then take the canine of which here is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle head into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed in forming the whole chain; do this often as long as all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey the application, stuff the cotton in the ear canal as I said for the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them treating the distillations; and distill your oils and your medicines in the ear to all this instrument, from which this is the form as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or of iron, narrow below to one small holes, and above open to distill; and for pressing inside the distillation one instrument of iron well made for this, and if you see take one razor and wrap around the point conveniently cotton; then throw your oil or your juice, and what you see of your medicines in the caine, and let the caine be in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be one pock heated over the fire thus when you distill them in the ear; and keep that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the Stoppings of Ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by the swelling of wounds, or by flesh growing inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes come from within the ear so one cannot see them; and sometimes they have i.e. a point of pus from the hole, and it is seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one which comes from within so that it cannot be seen, is of great healing in more positions, and for this reason you should put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening apparent, then the work has all this spatula from this.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it aged and trenchant before and behind all plain, so that it does not bleach the ear; if the opening is of flesh growing or bone of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, as long as that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the suppuration is in the ear, take a fine and light razor and heat it a little over fire, then place it in the body of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation that the patient feels keenly in the ear, pierce lightly, and take care not to strike the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment.  
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw out the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it as long as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bleeding which are or treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper of
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ointment that comes on papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, so it is necessary that you stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and the root with a spatula; then put on its place powdered vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it decorticate, so cauterize with the lenticular subtle cautery, and the cauterization after the incision is worth mutes; and many times they return, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	of the gristle
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come in papers the eyes some things that seem hard in its form and in its hardness, and for this reason this disease is called «granular», and it is an assembly of moisture thick in the paper above and below; the work is such: take ward if the granule moves from one side and the other, and it’s a light thing to know; then make the large donques, then the exfoliate of each part lightly, then take the tweezers, and the cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, do not grieve the patient; and if the fissure is large, assemble it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, for the flesh will restore it soon and engenders flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending in the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper, and holding the hail with tweezers, cut it and press on both sides; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it grieves nothing; and when the hail is cut, leave the eye of salt water, and cure the place with that which heals flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is made in the tissues of the papers above, and this happens more to children than adults, and grieves much to their eyes, and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces sideways, and sleep on top, and are their papers below their eyebrows moist that the inflammation and appearance have covered with exinach which opens in the eye.  
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your two hands and feel the exirnach between them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your palm; and then take one drapeil of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinarnach from each part, then place it on top; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinarnach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatula a trenching a slit of a width, and let it not be more than the wound that one makes to the vein; and make the skin apart as far as you come to the exinarnach; and in more dispositions comes exinarnach from the slit, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then a whole piece of cloth charpit between your fingers at the outside, and turn your hand to right and left as much as it is spread; and keep that you do not add into the slit, until you come to all the spatula up to the eye, that you do not blind him.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the opening does not open at the beginning of the fissure, then gently widen the fissure until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten bandages in oil and water, and place on the site, and restrain with bands.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind straw and put it on to corrupt the moisture which has lingered. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then care for him until he is healed. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place abscess hot, so its cure of plasters soothing until it is healed.  
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When on paper there grow hairs other than the natural ones, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes, and bring about many diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the eyelids and albuginea, so much that it is cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to .iiij. manners: either by cautery in all fire, or by medicine aqua according to what is before or chapter of cautery, and is done either by incision and stitching or by cauteries, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your healthy one, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, put an awl with .i. thread above; and be it below the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow beside these hairs, and pull .i. thread upwards to all the paper, and turn it back to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the added hairs, to all the spatula copying, from the large tear to the small one; then extract .i. thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then place on top of the paper a figure of an enclosure, as the myrtle leaf, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if to a person who needs it one cuts a large quantity of paper according to how the paper is softened; then make on the whole spatula above the two lines that you have marked, and start with a wide tear up to small; and let one of the splits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the scalpel in one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape all; then assemble the two lips with a seam of a needle with all the fine wool thread, and wipe the blood, and make air to the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows with none things sticky, if you see doing this; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the seam and the threads until three days or four; then cure the wound without a seam of dry and constricting things, because the paper revives to the bottom of the wound and the assembly of it, but the suture is moved (as they say the ancients), and this work without fear; and if in another way: and that you mark the paper with a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, three incisions unscrewed according to the form which is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut that which surmounts the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the power to hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, take a needle where it has thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put the other thread along the large tear, and the second thread along the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above what you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointment; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the wounds is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to what I have said, and then make .ij.  caines by art, and .ij.  subtile liens as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut the .ij. heads of .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on that which rises above the paper of the eye, and strain the .ij. caines of the .ij. parts forming; and let it remain thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and shrink and draw together, until it heals by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, if the wound is cut with force, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is sutured, and if the paper is removed, and they will no longer prick; and this is the form of the II canes that you shall make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works is such that you take a fine needle, and put into it 1 thread of silk soft and fine; then assemble the heads and tie one and the other finely, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order in the chase another thread of silk very thin, and tie the chief of the threads; then put the patient’s head on your own; and be facing the sun so that the work is clarified, because it is a subtle and fine work; then put the needle to all the chase in the root of the hair adjusted, and let it pierce into the paper hastily until you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put into the chase that hair, if there is 1 or 2 or 3 or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come forth to all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then you will draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes forth from the hole above and that you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows on it; and if the hairs are small, accompany it with 1 long hair of the natural ones, and be raised with that one or you leave it, as long as it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called 'aleacrati' or rot comes in the eye, if there are of two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by a sudden blow from a wound, or incision, or cautery, and by similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you split that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and lay it until it be healed; and it does not behoove that you use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than the first; but there is work of softening things, such as fennel; and the rose of water or ale and flaxseed are cooked, and diachylon ointment melted in any oil, and a tent is wrapped around it, and the cure is done with this. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure is that you take care that it does not close again according to the form that it was before; and these works that we have said are nothing but addresses of this illness, that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This sickness which is dislocation is truly called “axacrati,” and is both natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and fissure and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you prick an awl, in which it has the double thread, and place it in the cartilage, and let it pierce from the left tear to the right, so that the thread comes into the two shoulders of the cartilage; then hold the cartilage above the entire awl, and the cope at the spatula wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is fitting, it is good; if not, then take the razor and put it in the opening, and turn the paper, and make openings where it costs inside the paper; and let the heads of the two openings be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make angles so that when they are assembled, the figure is as similar to the figure of a letter which has the name “I grieche”; then remove the flesh, according to the quantity that its cost is pulled down below, from those who follow the paper, then adjust the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then care for what we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, as long as it is healthy. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the malady comes from a fissure or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the skin, and according to what is above; then bind between the two leaves of a tent, as I said; and one must do the work according to the form of the malady, because it is very diverse in form, and the sages masters equip everything with all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what it is necessary for work and instruments in more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the skin's surface
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens to a man's eye in such a manner that the skin above is glued with the white of the eye, and cannot move nor perform its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor under the skin, and raise it up; and while holding the tweezers, as long as you cut what is attached to the spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient does not suffer that the spatula too sharp nor bleaches the eye; and let your incision, by which you peel back this assembly, be slight, so that the skin returns to its natural form; and all this assembly is healed, and one never uses salt water in the eye, but rather sweet water, and honey; then put between the skin and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened with oil; and after the third day use the honey and things inward until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in two ways: it is nervous and similar to one hard silk, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and cured burns like pinches, it cannot be; and one and the other semblance begins towards the large tear, and crosses little by little until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and raise the paper with your hand, then coil the angle with a small doubleure, and lift it upwards; then take a needle, and put in it one hair of horse, or goat, or ox, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the angle, and pierce it all the way through with the needle, and tie the angle with a thread and lift it upwards, and scrape all around the edge of the angle that follows the prunele and silk to the hair until the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear with all the spatula subtle and as small forces, and leave the natural flesh or tear, so that through the incision the body of tears does not come as is accustomed; and no times lift the angle only once, and with the thread, as we have said; then scrape it all around the spatula like this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a little bit of crushed silk, and with the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it of what it needs until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerved, and you cannot put the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, it works the eye of the patient, and take the spatula lighter little sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not diminish and the reason is quick, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red collar and crushed silk, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as an abscess pouch, then milk it and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh near the tear duct bothers the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it with a thread, and cut away a portion but not too much that the flow of tears doesn't come; then distill in the eye red collyrium which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyes of some men are born sometimes red, and cover the eyelid and restrain over the papers and turn them to the outside, and it seems like a rose of bloom; and the work is that the patient puts his head into your healthy, then you open the eyes, and coil all that flesh with suitable needles to those, and sustain it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go on cutting until the end, and keep that you do not bleed the eye in the work; and be the incision of the spatula that we have said in the incision of the angle and as small forces of which one removes the shell, so like the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all flesh removed, then use the oil of seal ground or you distill red wine and similar medicines corrosive, and put over the eye a cotton with yolk of egg, so that it be assured of a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the blood does not come to the surface, and you doubt the hot abscess, then leave the eye and cure the abscess of things soothing a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as many layers are set in the eye by this way. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless, it is necessary that you heal the cure of each weak eye from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works as long as you see that this limb suffers that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red that are covered above the eye, and take from sight their work and weaken the eye all days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary that you first examine if the eye, in which it is, is, and nothing else is wrong, except for the eyeball; therefore, coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put their head on your hand, then suspend those veins along the entire body according to your wisdom, and let the incisions be subtle, double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two incisions be by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then with this coil you force those veins subtly, and wipe away the blood hour after another, until you see removing those veins outside of the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of spatulas, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, if you distill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrode what remains of the red vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to collect all these in that hour, so make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and let it for some days until the pains are appeased and be assured of hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before as long as it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula is called "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and medicine burning according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it should die, and treat all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and blackness, then the ruler has all the tools of this form; and it is called "sharp head," and be made from fire iron to one chief rounded, and be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on top the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little bit as long as you know that the corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place of drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is joined, and flesh grows, and the bowel's body is joined, and it remains thus for XL days, and it does not renew and is not at all an abscess, know that it is healthy; if not, there is no other means than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the vein according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take the iron in this shape, and let the head of iron be at III angles, and let the shaft be thinned until the top as you see here. 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it upon the bone beside the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn all the instrument until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through that which comes in this if he holds his hand on his cheek; and then restore the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the place, then the matter goes to the cheek; thus is lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open and there is no disturbance to the nose or lessening, then it behooves you to bind the patient; then heal, then put on suction cups or a haeretel without injuring to suck, then put on the eye  i. linen made of acaice and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye, and emplaster above with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths enough soft, and double each in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye has need; then bind it from above with a hard bandage, and restart the suction cups to suck without injuring; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the linen softens, then it behooves you to strain it much; then remove the linen after the day and night, and if you see the eye repairing, it is good; if not; then restart the emplastering and cloths and linen and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the dislocation of a linen cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear comes in the woven cloth, then open it and there come forth like i. grain of resins, and is expectable to see; therefore if you see it covered, the work is such that you put one needle in the root of the lower part until the upper one, then put another needle where there is i. double thread of the part of the seam; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the grape around, and restrain it well, then withdraw the needle and put the other half linen oil in abundance of an egg; and let it stay until the thread falls with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and at no time the wound is restrained by the grape each part of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great appearance, then pierce it with a fine spatula which comes from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and descend the eyes, and enter immediately; then withdraw it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bowel of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This sickness which is called «alcunnati» is not other than a bow that is assembled in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work so is that you make the patient sit on the prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands of II parts, and move it as long as you see the bow coming to the top to your eyes; then be ens fichie, and do not descend and be discombree the light, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not arranged as we have said.  
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sharp spatula and with it on the cornea touch  a point by continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the corona, as long as the bubble is there; and when it is out, pour distilled water hot mixed with honey, or water in which fennel has been boiled and honey, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of thorns of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of the eyes in division, and what is necessary to examine them; so work according to the healthiness.  
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and bind the healthy eye tightly; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument that is called "almagda," or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then put the point of the instrument next to the cornea by the width of a hair in that whiteness of the eye at the part near the tear duct, then push the instrument that is called "almagda" skillfully, and restrain your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that the almagda comes to the empty space; and it behooves you that the measure of the almagda's path be at the depth of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black; and this is the cornea of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then put the instrument up to where the liquid is, then squeeze it down one passage after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the water descends now, so the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.  
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest a little, and if the liquid returns by the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is in place and does not go up, gently withdraw the albuginea, turning your hand back and forth; and then put back into the eye a bit of silken thread, and leave out the oil inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by fire the oiled or moistened cloth in rose oil and in abundance of egg, and bind with the healthy eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on as common bread with an abundance of egg. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if "almagda" cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyes too hard, then it is fitting that you take the instrument which is called "alberit," of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep in its passage, but make it subtly, then put almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work equip the patient with a bed before, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be free from all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie it in the same dark house, and examine his sight, and let him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not fitting that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you tie it up, because the water rises quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess comes, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and the head of those who soothe the abscess; and when it is appeased, then unbind the eye and place upon its face the orilliet to cover for any day, and let it be under in that dark house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he goes out of the house here and there, and converts to his case; and know that none of disciples should interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almagda pierce, so that one sucks the liquid, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of the almond, for those who do not know them they see them; and be of rain properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of the wing of this same subtlety, and the last one in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the birth
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or made various horns joined together, so that some resemble scorpions with many feet; and if there are such and the horn has a skin of bad color, and also has skin of good color. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these chariots which is not wounded, and not broken, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open his nostrils, and throw the incense to those chariots, and the straw outside; then cut what you can hold with the fine sharp spatula on one side, until you know that the chariot is entirely removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be covered, open it entirely i.e., with instruments subtle and light, so that nothing remains; and if there is no swelling or abscess, cover it as it is proper; and if it is a malignant abscess, haste and cauterize it until the blood is extinguished and all the pus is removed, then apply either boiling water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is clean; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh in the bone above, so that the instruments cannot come to cut: therefore it is necessary that you put I linen thread a little thick, and be anointed with hands ours, and have between each nut I space; and put the patient's shoulder of the thread in his nose at its power, and pull in smelling until it comes by the nose inside the mouth; and many times children do so at school, and it is easy for him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes by the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and feel one after the other being as we are who are or thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do what you know that the new ones have corrupted that flesh, then treat the wound, wipe the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it straight back in its place as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the head a bandage of wool for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, for which one distills the oils and medicines in the head.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a can, and you lead it thus; and if you wish, make a closed can, and let the instruments be full to cleanse the head; and have i. handle at the top for holding it when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the birth
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
