Many times at the beginning of birth a sickness arises which is called "telul," and it grows and becomes large very quickly, to the point that it is a thing to behold; and for this reason it behooves you to cut it at the beginning, and pull out all the pus, then put on its place the cautery or medicine burning; and if one delays to cut it until it is large, beware, if it is hard, of dark color, with poor sensation; do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when one cuts it once, great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, and you see that it can be all cut out, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with things drying and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the birth is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilage works, it does little good, for in certain men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore when this happens to anyone, see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips together with a suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, then you must scrape all the parts of their core until they are healthy, then assemble the two lips together with a suture, and bind it, and put powder over powder of dragon’s blood, and ground incense; and put above the powders a piece of plasters of strong or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it dries by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have let you know.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To men's hands happen inside the lips abscesses hard, seeming to grains of vezis, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut on each knot, and take it with tweezers and cut it in every part; then apply there after incision of vitriol ground, until the blood is stanched; and then the leaf of aisil, and cure the place of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh is born on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and leave the wound open for the blood to flow; then put on the place vitriol ground, or other restraining and drying powders; and if this flesh returns after the incision, and often happens so, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; so you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and pull out the teeth or scabs appear, until nothing remains; and thus do of blackness and greenishness, and jaundice and other spots, until they are cleaned; and if one removes what is at the first reason, it's good; if those no, so it begins again the second day and the third, until you have all pulled out; and know that teeth need diverse forms of instruments to pull out, according to what the work shows you, because the scraper with which one pulls out outside the teeth have other forms than those with which one pulls between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait to draw as much as you can, because one must not do it hastily; for it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to remove.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to milk, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth aching. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the patient, and thinks that it is or tooth Saint, and make milk the good tooth; and nevertheless does not depart me the pain by this, as long as the evil is strained, because we have already wanted to do so to these saints; and when you are well certain of the tooth ailing, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth all its. a spatula hard for warder the gum from all sides; then the moves to your two or tongs subtle in the first place and place, as long as it is well dislodged, then i firm well the tongs; and be the head of the patient on your saint between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is extracted straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and put it gently into each side, and move it as you did before.  
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it is necessary that you fill it with bandages, where the holes are; and hold it gently with tweezers so that it does not break when you pull it; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And therefore take good care that you do not break it, and that a part remains, and returns to the patient through the wickedness of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard that you do not act as the ignorant doctors do, who by their haste and boldness break sometimes the bone, and bring them not what we have recounted; but cause often by the incision of these great ills for the roots that remain there, or for the bone that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or oil and salt; and if blood comes from the wound, which often happens, apply vitriol powder to it; and if this does not work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, to what one moves the teeth first, be long points and big handles, that they do not double when you will draw the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be big members so that they do not bend when drawing, and be of well-made iron, and be toothed for better holding.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the teat, it is necessary that you place upon it cotton moistened with butter for a day or two. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the eye is still moist, then put in the forceps that are called "algebri," so that the shoulder appears like a bird's beak; and be made inside like a file and this is its shape: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say, a spatula, because of this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root leaps out with those, it is good; if those do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front in the shape of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it may not break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not numbered; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others; and if one breaks not the bone of the horse or of other bones, as it can, then he seeks the instruments that are necessary, that I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove; and then return to its place of medicines suitable for those, and if it has in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and even in virgin women, then it befits that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file or trim it; therefore the edge; and if it is near with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to a small beak, and let it be of pointed iron at the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping a little bit each day for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can file it, so the file of a certain form as this is:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file of which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little each day lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks; then the plain at the end to nothing a scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and it pierces the tongue, so it is necessary to file the sharpness so that it is equal, so that it does not pierce the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth loaches, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that he can chew without it hurting, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and this does not work; if so, it is necessary to restrict it with a thread of gold, because the silver thread becomes green and rotten, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too fine nor too coarse, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth are crooked, then take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the jaws between the teeth that have fallen out, if there is one or more, until you wisely come to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin again the covering until the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.  
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the ends of the wire with pliers and bring them together, and put them between a healthy tooth and the broken one, and place it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it like this as tight as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the wires are broken, restrain it with another wire; let it remain and serve like this until the end of its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two broken ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, fresh against fresh, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and patient should intervene, and sometimes the form of a tooth made from bone of walrus is made, and it is placed in the place where the defect is, and it is restrained as we have said, and remains and serves in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No times is this ligament that comes from under the tongue or nature, that one is born thus; or by accident of a wound joined; and the works are such that you work the mouth of the sick, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve ligament wide, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or something else, and it is from the closing of a wound, so put the awl and cut wide that ligament; and guard that the cut be not too deep, for the artery that is underneath; and when you have done, raise the place with rose water and honey, or with cold water, then put under the tongue a linen tent; and bandage the sick each night, that the place cannot join. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, put on the place ground vitriol; and if the blood does not stop, then cauterize it with the lentil cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a fiery color or black or hard, so that the sick person does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, put the awl and make it with a fine spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the bleeding persists in your work, put vitriol ground on it until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you draw all out; then raise the head with honey and salt, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come within the throat bumps which are called “godath,” and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if it is a hard abscess of little size and yellowish color, do not touch it with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the bleeding; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will cut it off, or it would break by itself; and if it is white in color, and the root is thin, have your instrument prepared to cover it, but first see if the abscess chafes and rests. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit facing the sun, and his arms be on his waist, and he opens his mouth and the surgeon places the instrument between his hands, and presses the tongue down with all the instrument, this is the form; and it is of silver or fine steel like a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, so take the oncine and stick it in the almond, and draw it forcefully upwards as much as you can; and do nothing of the fabrics with it, then cut with the instrument, from which is the form, that seems like forces; but anyway the chief are bent, and one place to the other, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron or d'andainne:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut with pliers, from which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be trenching on one side and the other side name; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and thus, and if decorrement of blood happens, so gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed; then cure it until it is healed; and some times other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them as you did the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman of an abscess that was within her throat, that is to say the abscess of small size; and I had well nearly closed the whole throat, so that the woman could not expire through the passage which was stopped up, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high raised that it had been necessary to put two fingers through each of the two openings. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then did this, and put one in the one incision, then pulled out the thread, and in drawing a large portion of the bowel; then I refixed another piece in the other part of the two, and I opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; after I put the incision in these abscesses, and scraped a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus was cleared the woman's throat conduit, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I burned it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stayed without growing; and I left those parts, and know only that God did to her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the stem grows upward to the grape, and it is swollen and long, it is called “perpendicular”; and if it is very large and rounded, it is called “grape”. 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the pus of the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it; and the one which is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of fusse color or black, then it is necessary that you avoid the incision of it.  
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril to the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It therefore behooves you, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we have made mention of before; then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it downwards, and the probe to the II instruments that I have said in the incision of the II almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it grieves to the voice, and to speech; and after the incision, use those things that we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it as long as it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears to be cut, then you must use an instrument for the cauterization of the senses that cause fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head on your healthy side, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said in this chapter of cautery, and confines with a very sharp knife, so that it be not too thick nor too bright; and in employing the end of this instrument, because this is its form:  
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place on his head a hair or one puts the medicine, as the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine on the uvula; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscles come from his mouth of the medicine within, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the palate; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it on the uvula, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it burn and the incisions of the medicine be appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it on any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the canal above, until the cotton adheres on the uvula; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and fall after .iiij. days or .v.. And if you have need to begin the cauterization of the medicine again, then begin it again, and after the cauterization, wipe around the uvula, with cotton dipped in butter, and purify what is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calamint and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in 1 pot, and put it inside, and boil it; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have 1 instrument of hair according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it silver or lead, and let one of the heads be put in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the grape through the vein, until the grape is mortified; after that it often recommences, until the grape dries, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the arrival of the hot abscess, because many things happen; and do not do this except at the decline of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a canine and put inside its head a wick of wool, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the wick of wool does not make the vapor hurt the mouth, and it is good cure together salvation.  
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or spine of fish, or any thing, gets stuck in the throat; so it behooves you to draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, it behoove you to make the sick person vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it will expel the thing through vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or 1 mouthful of dry bread; and tie to the sponge 1 thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will get stuck, and then you draw it out further; and if it does not come out through what we have said, then take 1 instrument of plank according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all of life come to it, nor push in the bone; and move it better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows whether it is well or the thing is difficult; so he pushes down, or pulls it up with all the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the throat's bleeding
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	At no time is medicine given to the bleeding patient, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun, then that you press his tongue with the instrument that I told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the suture, then treat it with all the small pincers, or with subtle pliers that are good for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not enough, take a heated iron and put it in the throat of the patient, then put the end of the iron where the hair is hot, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient hold water all day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full a glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and put it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he will spit. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida using the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, because it will fall without harming. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot or it has burning coals in it, and let the cover be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that one put the head of the instrument; then you put your fumigation there, and the patient puts the head of the cauldron in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes until the nostril; and the nostril will now fall, and if it does not fall, begin the fumigation again many times; and endure thirst, and drink salty and sour things, and do not drink water; and then the matter is necessary that it is done through this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument that is used to treat the sinus is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pliers so that they can enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has sharpness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many resemblances of abscesses are, according to those that memory comes here after from one and the other in this book, and are diverse in perforation and in size; and it is in II manners where one is in its own likeness, and of those which it holds moisture. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the wounds which are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscess of the head is other than that of the foundation, and the abscess of the fleshy part is other than that which comes in the joints, and each has its judgment in the work.  
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one should not cut until the boil is ripe according to its fulfillment; and if to some that it is necessary to cut when they are crude, and do not die according to their fulfillment, like abscesses that are near joints.  
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and one lets it remain as long as it is rotten and swollen, by chance, the ligament and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is why there is contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay piercing it until it is mature, it will harm the principal limb; when it is near the foundation, pierce it so that it may ripen; and it is not proper that you pierce an abscess before complete digestion, except for the one which is near the foundation, lest it pour forth, and become elongated inside, and a fistula comes; and it cannot heal in a long time.  
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is mature according to its accomplishment, and it is when the pain is appeased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and of the redness, and of the swelling and of the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where more dependent the place of the abscess, and where it appears to open; and be the perforation of the long one of the body, and if the abscesses are on the hands or on the feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no pliability.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that are displaced by following according to which limb. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it's good that you leave the perforation as long as it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.  
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce him before these, the body of his venom will become elongated and is full of much filth; and by chance it hardens the lips and the depths of him. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limbs have need.  
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to remove the core, and cover; when it has become as if a sheet, and is withered, then it is necessary to do as with boils; and if there are such that are cut in III angles, and if there are such that one covers like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the angles; and if there are such where one makes a round size, and other sizes and seeming cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who has no head, as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it plainly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, if you do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain one part; then plug the abscess until the other day, then drain nothing directly; do this many times from great to great, until the pus is gone completely; same for if the patient is of feeble strength, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old men decrepit.  
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes escapes with the exit of the bowels, which by chance may kill the patient, and you should not be concerned about it.  
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, then wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat incision, then administer bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put in each one a bandage so that it comes against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have covered it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen without moisture, and tie it up until the third day; then bone, and cure with ointment until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, so administer cold water and ease, and moisten the bandage, and put it on the place bleeding many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, it should be administered government and care, and the powders that I have said in this book by hand, and if it is wintertime, and the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is summertime, and the wound is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on cloths moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as is proper, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is important to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of  the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where near the head come small abscesses, and are mannered of us that are in webs, as like the bush of a vine, and much in them are similarities. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such that have moisture like the legs; and there are some which are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act against it.  
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are that you should experience to all instrument which is called "entromissoire," of which its form comes after, what it contains.  
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then it is dried by means of a long cloth. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is dried, then carefully scrape without leaving the hair that contains that moisture, because it returns as soon as one leaves it nothing; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain dry should be cleaned.  
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resumes the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain in any of it; then cure the wound with ointment suitable to it, until it is healed.  
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in fat, then cut according to this form, long; and put your knives there, and scrape it from all sides, and put all your care to drain the pus where it lies; and if the artery goes against you, then do what I have told you after.  
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do with an abscess if it is purulent, and of cutting and curing as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on a pus-filled abscess and moist one is easier, because they contain little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in some of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and of these fut I abscesses that I opened or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and cannot be broken; and if one had made any incision on it, one would have done just as well as with a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, where those that come to the chief of children and to the roots of ears, the opening should be always at the most dependent point, in order to let out the pus; and the treatment as it is proper. 
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come from other parts of the body, and they are bad, and they are intertwined with each other. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its side, like the boil and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similar appearances to these scrofulas. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some that do not want to obey health.  
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that therefore that you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not harsh to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not too deep; so it is necessary that you cut it from above, and the peel from each part, and are the II lips of the heart as ones, if you have need of it, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and the treat prick and prick, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and not be the spatula too thick nor trenching, that the hand does not escape, and see too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put vitriol powder, or any powders that stop blood, in the wound, and restrain the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to purr. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stanched, return to your work, until you have completed it; then examine with your index finger if there are any small scabs, and cut them and cleanse them.  
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has in the root of the scrofulous vein a great one, it is not necessary that you cut that scrofulous at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it, without annoyance; then apply the wound of old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, because there is no delay of superfluity for the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	So it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and to suck out pus, and then cauterize as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce where it opens more; and pierce it like the one before said, in depending, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is left of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then the cure of ointment preventing flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	of a hernia
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land who did it, and this is the scripture of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinance, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cut; and one should not help them, because all the veins and the arteries of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two cheeks.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the artery, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below III circles or IV with a small incision across, between the II circles or by the quantity of the incision of the syfac, nor in the cartilage; and these are so suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from within. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it conviene that he extend the skin of the throat to all the neck, then cut the keel as long as it comes to the windpipe; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and demonstrate by the section of the phlegm of the windpipe that it flows from where it is broken, and by the defect of the voice; and leave the wound open a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed from which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew them together alone against the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one does not do this until the throat is completely choked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect comes from the lung.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, cover the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are guarded from death; and for this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease is passed, and it is passed in III days or in IIII. And then they commanded to sew the wound and cure it, as long as it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took the knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called by her to cure her, and I found her as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and so well that it had not cut a vein nor led further than the throat, and the wind was blowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I bandaged it, and so I treated the wound until it was healed; and it happened to the young lady that she was hoarse in voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition; for this reason I say that in cutting the epiglottis there is no fear.  
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of a wound, and it is very common in women; and it is according to II manners: natural, and accidental; where nature does not have an engine. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to us fat, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear in it, and it does not become work to do forcibly except in this one who is small, and proves and searches the whole introducer: if you find it as I fat, and cannot to any vein, so cut it, as one cuts the us, and treat it throughout its entire head, if there is any; and enclose well all, and cure it as it should, until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are ours, of which I will say all the appearances; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between us and issue. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that out is sometimes and fever holding, as long as the boil is not passed, and is accomplished the putrefaction; therefore rests the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new one there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the syphilis, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a blister, and becomes large; and they are according to two appearances, whether fat or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the wound, that you examine and inquire first of all about the instrument called "entromissoire," according to what its form will come or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses as we do is that you prick or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the introducer, and take care in those that leap further. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs short, whatever color it has, make it as I have said of other abscesses; and if after the probe there comes no moisture, know that it is fat, so make it in a cross, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape it on each side and ward the coat where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the root; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, so drain it in pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it does not remain there, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little, and the wound does not grieve you, apply to the wound some corrosive powders sharp, and restrain the wound, and put on above soothing things,  a hot poultice, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the swelling is great, stitch the two lips of the wound, and cure it as someone who forms flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beating is contrary or otherwise if you are in haste and apply the place of ground vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound is rotting, and rests the boiling of blood; then return to cover those that remain from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of instruments for introduction, and they are in III ways: large and medium and small; and there are III squares that are called "albaret", and I which is called "breb", and there are in III ways: large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula; and they are also like needles with which one sews the sorceress's wounds, and they are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth it most, and they are more proven by black plum for surrounding the fistulas' corbeurs; and they are in III ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.  
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the tongs are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are tongs that have II curves in III ways also; and there are tongs that have III curves, and are also in III ways; and there are tongs that have II curves, and tongs of a single curve only, and are in III ways; and all of these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these tools is sharp, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, which we skin the flesh with so that we do not cut the vein or the nerve; and these instruments are probes put back in handles so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of the abscesses; and they are three ways: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another smaller instrument, resembling finger picks, according to this form, to which we bleed.  
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at no time in the place that is healthy for opening of veins and arteries, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form from this line b. up to g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh growth, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitching, and care for it until it is healed; and if the swelling becomes larger, as women have it, make two incisions above, in similar fashion; so that one holds the other at the end of each, such that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.; then scrape the skin which is between the two lips and remove the fat, and apply there what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the care, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the loss of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it drains the remaining part and fat, then care for it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous nodules in which there is pus.
