Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore who contain moisture ought to be cut according to this form, from the line .b. until the line .g.: 
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole core that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply to the wound some old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment as before to it until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like the appearance of scrofulous sores, then make it as we have said in cutting open scrofulous sores, and if the wound enters inward, administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the artery rupture
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin above it is stitched together, then many times abscesses come; and just as often it happens to a vein that is swollen and has an abscess; and if one knows whether this is because of the artery, then the abscess is long in shape; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a pulling sensation; and when it is because of the vein, then there are red streaks appearing; and it is folly to cover this abscess, even when it is beneath the armpits and elbows and neck and many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It behooves therefore to shun the cure of iron, and he who is at chief behoove also to shun, and in that which is inflamed by artery making from above the skin with long; then work the size as incisions, and depart beautifully the artery of the cloths, until it is discovered; then put below it a needle, and make it pierce up to the other side, and extract the artery of a double thread in II leagues, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries which are in temples; then point the place which is between the II links of an intromissoire until the blood that is there issues, and be it delieze the abscess; then administer the cure that enjanre bowe, as long as the link hangs; then cure those of ointment following to those, until it is healthy; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, so it behoove that you hold in your hand that which you can of the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle below the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there is I double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or link of one of II parts as II chiés of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads are not issued, so I put back another needle to all I thread below all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and extract the threads in IIII leagues; then cut the abscess until the superfluities there issue, then cut the superfluity of the keur and leave that which is tied; then put on top I drapeil moist in wine and oil, then administer it cures of tents and ointments as long as it is healthy. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses also come in the nerves when they are  worn out, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips and in all their joints, and it is grief abscesses, and its color seems the color of the body, and is in more dispositions without pain; and when one restricts it forcibly, the patient feels pain, and is not well throughout the body, but below the heart; and moves well from all sides, and does not go neither forward nor backward, nor down nor up, and those who are in the joints should not be covered with iron: lest there might be contraction; and those who are on the head or forehead, make the skin to a spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, take it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it to the winch, and flay it, then clean and gather the wound together with sutures, and dress it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	Of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and nowhere else, and is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to them, and the roots are subtle, and the head is large; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and they had fine roots, and they were slightly split, and pus flowed from them. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI З., and the work in incision is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of subtle root; if it cuts with a broad spatula, and be in your presence the cautery to fire.  
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist there often come too great discharges of blood, and if the bleeding does not stop, then hasten quickly to cauterize it; and if you see that the patient is fearful and frightened by the incision of iron, then take a thread of lead well made, and tie it around the limb as we have said, and leave it for days; and then restrain it, and do not cease from restraining the thread of lead until it closes the limb, and heals itself without effort; and if the roots are thick, you may be afraid to cut them even with the belly, but you may well cut half, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and keep that you do not cut the tendon which is of pale color and poor sensation and milky looking.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess festering, and I will come to the cure of syphilis later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the skull is moved
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from cautery of a wound or fissure in the skin, and is on the belly and has some bubbles, like they have in other sores, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was said before, or of wind; and if it is due to the rupture of the fistula and the exit of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens through diverse outlets. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is because of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with his hands, it returns up, and then comes back down, and perhaps it is closed, and grows greatly at the entrance of the bath and for strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is for blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses large and hard, and are fixed according to an amount; and if it is for windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look at its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you should leave the care. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, so it behooves you to command the patient that he keep his arm, and be outstretched straight, then place a cloth all around the belly; then command him to grip hard between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the abscess above all the great incision; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the wound be closed with the linen; then operate the half of the abscess extended over the linen, and put your index finger, and search the intestine; if you find it caught by the linen, so untie it, and put the intestine out of the belly's exit; and if you find the bowel, so take it at the incision, and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery makes it contrary, or the vein, so go well around, then return to your work and take II needles, and put II strong threads, and put the II needles around what you have done in a cross that you make piercing; then strain the abscess in IIII leus on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it will rot, and let the dead flesh fall away by itself; or you cut it when it is subtle and rotten, then cure it of what it behooves, and close the abscess as we have said; and strain the blood or the moisture that you find, then cure the place of what it behooves, and solder the place. 
dou chancre	Of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of ulcers, and how one must work them by medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and let us say the ulcer is prevented in the marshlands, and great caution should be exercised in its treatment, and ancient ones said that when an ulcer is in a place where one can shave it like an ulcer which is on the breast, and in the hip, and in similar places, and one must remove it entirely when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not proper that you approach it, because I have never been able to heal any of them; nor has anyone ever healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion; then make the patient's good bed to perform the operation; then lay your forceps or ulcer, and shave it on all sides, and take away everything completely without leaving anything behind; and let the blood run out entirely, and gently press the place with your hand or any object, and if the bleeding from the wound goes against the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it as long as the bleeding is extinguished; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; so it is only illuminated; and one should not touch iron in these two likenesses: that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this likeness of dropsy which is called "illuminated" with medicines, and the cure does not profit, look if the sick person is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as coughs and diarrhea and similar things; if you do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the sick person of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus operate: lift the sick person upright on your hands, and the minister presses the belly pushing the water to the lowest part under the ribs, then take the spinous spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be it cut from two parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, and all ways be not so deeply that it can come to the intestine when one puts it in, and do not be able to pierce it; then see if the hydropsy is engaged towards the intestines: if it is necessary that you fends above the bud III two right below the armpit; and if the hydropsy is for the disease of the liver, so be your cut on the left side of the bud III two; and if it is for the mucus, so be it to the right, and it does not befit that the patient lies on the cut that the superfluities do not run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and put it in, and raise your hand to all the spatula between the skin and the syfac as much as when you are scraping at the quantity of a nail or so; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the height of eight, and this is the place of the water, then take the water out, and put back this instrument because it is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a silver needle, and is of iron or archant light, and in the lower part I has a small hole; and on one side, III holes; and II on the other; and I on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision with which the scribes cut the feather. 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it descends now upon the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than it should in that hour, by chance the patient may die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is held now by the heart which stops the passage that is on the syfac, for this I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin the instrument again the other day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and treat from the point a little quantity; do this any day, and guard yourself from flooding until there remains no more than an amount of blood.  
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and give him much water, so cure of burial or hot sand, and with sweat or bath and sun, and he is to drink; and cure of drying medicines until it be healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without any holes in their penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary immediately he must look at all of the small spatula according to this form:  
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or pierce the thin cloth plug, and tie it and keep it so for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug, and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed.  
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose wound is small, so is medicated with the clove of plank, as we have said, if it will enlarge. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the penis in its place are blue, because none are born with the penis at the head of the shaft, for that reason they cannot urinate before they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot come to the urethra, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies supine on his back, with the head of the penis and the scrotum raised as high as a feather, so that the opening is in the middle, as it should be; and guard against bleeding which often comes, and if it happens, let him who stanches blood stanch the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the blisters of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters come to this [area] of the penis, and is a loathsome appearance of flesh; and there are malignant ones and non-malignant ones; so it behooves you to prick them with .i. one subtle needle, and scrape and clean all of them, then put on cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of bad colour and pus-filled, then you must apply a cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have it caught, and if the nail is in some on the handle, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the nail which is inside first; and when it is joined, then you cure the one outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cure it together, make sure the head of the stick is not pierced, and blackening and corruption come in its stick and groin; so it is necessary to shave off everything that is black and corrupt, then lay on top a plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranates and chickpeas, then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help with two kinds of disorders: namely, the letting of blood, and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary that you put or lead a chain of lead into the penis, and urinate on the patient; and when the skin is pierced at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with a sharp instrument, until the threads are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if this is a painful thing to consider, then it is necessary that you scrape it with a spatula any point at the head of the penis and of the skin; then pull gently between the two, and put there a fine linen cloth moistened in cold water, so that it does not dry out. 
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the separation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our will, and properly on children, then it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have no more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen the most part of the masters and healers who did circumcision around one [inch], and with force, and to all a new knife; so it was good because there are two layers, and by chance if one chops above and remains the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is better to cut and the pain is doubled, and at the purification which is around one inch [of distance from the glans] the point of the member is not guaranteed; and at the purification of the angle by chance the iron escapes, and the work is spoiled, and many times they are born such that they do not need purification and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification which is made with forces to the whole line of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut justly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, so it be equal in I whole soul tens; but that the thread be well strained around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be as that thou makest think to the child, if he understand, that thou make him only tie the thread around the staff so much, and then make him rejoice in all manners that thou canst; then make him rest between your hands straight, and raise forces between your hands or below your feet that the babe does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the staff and blow or heart, and draw it upwards until the head of the staff be in; then cleanse well of the filth which is assembled there, then tie the place signed with a double thread, then tie below I poc a the other lien; and hold as II dois by the second ligature to the pouch and the index finger, and cut between the II liens, then raise the heart upwards gently and draw the head of the staff; then let the blood run drop by drop, for it is the cure; and put powder on top and on top of the powder the drapeil glued with a piece of egg cooked unsweetened with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and cure him from other cure until he be healed. 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces in the unification thus is this: the two shoulders should be held and be sharp, and the shoulders also as large as the palms equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the unification is when the kernels inside are at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the leaus make an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with tweezers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they trespass three days, and what is below the rod is swollen, let it be so until the abscess has calmed, and the scab slightly; then cut it as you can move, and keep away from the part of the rod, it will not hurt him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place of things suddenly wound powder, that we have said or treated of powders, and if one cuts out too much, and it goes above, it will do no harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of urine retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or blood congealed, or a bowel, or new flesh, or similar things, that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone which is at the neck or opening of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the upper part above his back, and restrain the patient’s legs as much as he can; and therefore the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer an extraction with all the instrument which is called “syringe,” of this shape: and let it be of silver thin and light like the feather of a bird; and let the handle be a palm long and a half, and let it be fine at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it at the top of the piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the mound; then put the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient come to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order for that by whom it conducts or where it goes is twisted; then stretch the thread all over the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then withdraw it, and make the urine correct; and recommence the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scrapes or blood come in the bladder, or rot is gathered there, and you see it distilled with sharp waters and medicines, so do to all the instrument that is called "clepsedre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and if it has III openings: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the ends of the [chevez] because the medicine should be such that it stops the rod well without addition, if one can drain the moisture, and expel when necessary; and when you see to put your medicines in the bladder, put the chief of the catheter into the moisture, and draw with the [drawing instrument] that is inside; so draw the moisture to the catheter, and then firmly push back the [instrument] inside; so the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: here it is: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of archut, and it is the head higher; and below at the breast where the chains fall; then take a bladder of sheep and put in it the moisture that you see to clysterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a double fine thread, and heat the point of the clyster on the fire; then put the head of the clyster into the rod, then strain your hand on the bladder with all the moisture happening, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put the strong thread into these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dal, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as reins, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work with a size; and in the bladder, and in the member; and I will tell it to you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and it appears harene, and grieves the patient his member, and he can many times, and then urinates; and with much of these jumps the foundations; and it is light the healing of the children until they have four years, and it is very grievous in old people, and it is as the middle to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter of those who have the large stone, than of those who have the small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by clyster, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.  
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For he often hinders seeking the stone.  
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and dislocate and move them down so that the bladder descends to the middle of the leg, and it comes out once from its high place; then make him sit between your hands properly, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder be entirely declining downwards; then bring and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at touching the whole, moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man; and put it in its foundation, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, push it toward the neck of the bladder; then press on top with your finger, and push it out to where you want to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the scrotum upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the scrotum in the part where the incision is made; then put the spatula cutting, for this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between those that are between the buttocks and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be right above the stone, and your two sides should be either foundation or top, and let the waist be cut so that it is wide outward, and inward narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too big; by adventure press the two sides that are foundation or top, that she may come out without work; and know that there is such a stone where there are angles, and margins: if it is wounded, go over it; and if there is one like a gland, and round, whose issue is light.  
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To whoever has angles and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not open, then it is necessary that you extract it with the pliers which are like a file at the top, to force the stone out so that it does not escape; or you put under it a subtle instrument bent at the top; and if you cannot manage it thus, enlarge the hole of the opening, and if it does not open, strain it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove the larger, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be cut open, and make a larger wound. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes back through where the leaks cannot be soldered; but nonetheless, you must strive to drain it, or to debride with forceps, until you have extracted it in pieces; and when you have accomplished your work, you apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put on top a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, in order to appease the hot abscess; then suture the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, thoroughly wash the area with oil and water, then treat it with diaphicon ointment and basil ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and by this retained urine, which is known in such a manner that without jumping with the urine: therefore you must put in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and burn it; then raise the wound from water and ash and seal, and help him in all ways that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all hours that you cure him, you bind his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on top of the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the duct of the urethra leads, and fixed within, and the urine cannot flow; so the cure of what I say thus, that you cut it many times, is excused from cutting through this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tested this thus.  
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron forest according to this form and be it at three angles fitted into one twig:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then thrust the forest in the shaft lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the forest in your hand on the stone point by point, as long as you can feel the stone from the other side; soon thereafter will come the urine, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken at once, and jumps with the urine, and the patient heals; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one string below the stone and the other above, then make the rod go into the stone between the two strings, then pull it out, and untie the string, and purify the congealed blood which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stones of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens sometimes that a stone is in women, and if it happens at any time, the cure is grievous, and is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-knowing who reveals herself to the eyes, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the woman's stone is more deep than the man's stone, so it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear there is. And if necessity demands this, then it is necessary that you take a midwife well knowing, and with care find one, and if you cannot find one, then no need to cast mire subtle; and present her a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command her from the inquiry of the stone; and look very well if the woman is a virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her buttocks or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain her below her buttocks, and recommend her that she put her buttocks on the sick person, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder forming. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it is felt appearing, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move its (the) two above the stone or below, and let the tail be at first small; then put the point into the waist, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as much as the stone can exit, and know that many types of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have reins.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the resemblances to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone does not give way, then put vitriol powder on it, and hold it there for an hour until the stone is stained; then return to your work, as long as the stone is firm, and have instruments that I told you in the extraction of stones for men to aid you in your work; and if the stone does not give way, and it is the artery that is cut, then put the powder on the wound and strain with strips and bandages, and do not begin again, and leave the stone and do not touch it, lest the patient die; then cure the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the wounds are healed, then return to your work, as long as the stone is gone.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquatic ramice is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is from the heart of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is i.e. another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have se poc non.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes from the testicles, and is spread that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: whether it is declining to jaundice, or red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more; and these are the signs of knowing this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, I long like the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess re-occurs with a part of the egg, and for this reason people think that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white syfac, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, suspect all the intromissoire quarreit, of which the form is before.  
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the fullness of his body; then he lies on his back, on something a little high, and puts under him a lot of cloths; then sit on his left side, and command the minister that he sits on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the breasts; then take the spatula straight, and cut the skin of the breasts among them as long as near the armpit, and let the incision be completely straight, separating the skin of the breasts up to the white fascia, and scrape it subtly according to your power; then pierce the white fascia full of water at the wide opening, and extract all the water, and then put your tweezers, and raise the white fascia; and do not touch the heart of the breasts, but only the fascia; cut the whole or by pieces equally well, that if you do not cut it well sagely, it will return the water; and if the wound is a success in your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work of the fascia; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the breasts to one suture, then cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the ulcer corrupted by another malady, then it behooves you to tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flowing of blood; then cut the boil at all its suspension, and draw out the ulcer, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part as you have done with the first evenly, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wounded place half-wool soaked in rose oil; and put outside another wool soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two pads, and put on top of them doubled cloths, and tie it on above all the linen according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two drapelz, and use them of wool fleece according to this semblance and be assembled by stitching in the groin of the breeches, and one of the shoulders pricks onto the foundation up to the back, and the other on the side of the armpit; and the other two chiefs above the two angles, and be all assembled the restraint in the loop of the braier; and sometimes is medicine this ramice of cautery in place of iron size, and it is that you prick the cautery cultellar fine, and cut the leather of the testicles, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac that contains the liquid is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at once, and scorch it with this subtle cautery hot. 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the wound in all ways that you can, as long as you are scraping everything; and guard that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salved; and moves guarding against a decrease of blood, and movements that the works of size; and if nothing else makes you contrary, or abscesses or bleeding or another thing, so cure what makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.  
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, administer a perforation as I tell you, and when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that the watery root is there, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below with all the spatula wide, and put the perforation deep into the body; and let the opening be wide, so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and leave to flow the remaining water, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to issue from the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you put a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water of the hydrophics, of which the form is before; and enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or until then, and when it is assembled as before, and thus will pass the days of the patient.  
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many dispositions, for which it seems to me that one should leave it alone; and I will tell you about the work and appearances of an abscess.  
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and even to the genitals; and this is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by superfluity sour and acute, which is spread to the groin, or by percussion; and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and does not find any pain, and is a painful abscess; and perhaps are some abscesses grievous fearful and stony, and of dark color, and sometimes comes from out of an artery, or from the swelling of a vein.  
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by the artery's vein, so it is known by the arrangement of the hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it does not behoove that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from the swelling of a vein is known by his disposition to the expression of the touch of both hands, and one can well make the incision on this semblance, and on the other parts; and it is that you cut the core of the coins, then the egg being at the top, and the white part thereof be extracted, and deliver the suspensory from all sides of the egg.  
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already softened with these new vessels, then you should draw out the egg and cut it; and if it is adhered to the syringe or in that which is within the vessels, then you should deliver all of that membrane and cut it roundly.  
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the shaft is or its rear, then it behooves you to cut it entirely, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the works are completed, apply the wound to wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then dress it with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering resembling a lambskin, with the softening of the boils, and the patient groans when he walks; and the cure of this illness is as fearful as before, but nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then put the suspensory from the groin to your two hips, and all the vessels which are near the penis, and cover them with the masters, and extend them; then cut with a sharp spatula wide through the middle of the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then peel them on each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in temples; then put an awl where it has the double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein has come, and tie it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and drain the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as with others where one injures a bow, so that no vessel bleeds that nourishes one of the groin; for by this there comes no evil, and if to all the vessels comes blood, it is necessary to drain the groin on all the vessels; so that the veins do not lose their nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be helped.  
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are by the section that comes or there it is, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, so the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the buttocks; and this rupture is either at the side or from the extension of the, and come these II manners of wound from causes: or by percussion, or by jump, or by fall, or by lifting of heavy burdens, and by similar things; and the signs when it is of the extension of the , are that there is a ache and ache, in long time, and does not come suddenly; and is the abscess even up to the parfont, for that the  pushes the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the pus, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscess appears diversely, under the skin near, and this is for the issue of the intestine and the body outward from the pus.
