Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines with the abscesses, and are held in, and cause great pain to suffer the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron there is fear, because it befits to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to pull the intestine into his hand within the wound, if he can enter it; then be supported on his neck between your hands, and raise his hips; then keep the heart above, and cut all the skin of the buttocks long; then put inside the folds of the waist needles according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the eyes can go out; then scrape the soft tissue that is below the skin of the buttocks, until the white soft tissue is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger into what follows the buttock, in what is between the white soft tissue that is below the skin of the egg, and between the second soft tissue, and depart from what is behind the egg, and between the second soft tissue; and then move with the right hand inside the heart of the buttocks, and keep the white soft tissue on top to your left hand, and raise the egg onto all the soft tissue toward the waist; and instruct the minister that he extend the egg upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament; and ask with your thumbs if there is any intestine wrapped or white hard soft tissue, and if you find any of these things, put it into the belly below; then take a needle which has a thick thread made of X threads, and put it in the back part of the soft tissue, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the waist, then cut the chiés that appear from the threads, until there are IIII threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the soft tissue, of which we have said that it is below the skin of the buttocks, with a strong tie of II parts; then wrap the chiés of the threads, and tie them together in form of II parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter within, except an abscess may come; and put the tie straight according to the first long tie II thumbs of that one, and after these II ties leave the soft tissue which is below the heart of the buttocks the width of a thumb; and after all the other one according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the buttocks, as much as the sinew and the bow, as we have said before; then put moistened wool in oil, and put it in the wounds, and put the tie that we have said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is cauterized the white groin that we have said, after the incision, out of fear of a decrease in blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the linen until it is dripping through it; and if it delays in drying, so be raised with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it dries; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this matter, I never saw anyone daring to cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch which is assembled to the vine, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of those who work, as long as the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healthy. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture comes in the groin as we have said, and opens the parts; and no intestines come out to the parts, and if any do come out, it is little, and heals every hour; and nevertheless if it remains too long in this point, then the wound or syphilis grows, until the intestine comes out; and this happens because of the extension of the syphilis which is in the groin as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and swollen the parts and opened; and the cure is by cautery as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and that is the patient lies soundly on his back between your hands, then cut the part of the rupture inflated wide according to the quantity of III fingers; and then extract the syphilis which is under the skin that the one inside, then take the rait and put it on the place appearing of the syphilis; and press it in the fullness of the belly, then sew the II parts appearing of the syphilis on the head of the rait, and sew the one and the other; then extract the head of the rait, and do not cut the syphilis nor extend the one or other thing as I have made you know in the cure of the ramice of the intestines; then cure by the cure of the wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, if it defiles and cures the wound, as long as it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The back is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the genitals
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the genitals is softened in some men, because the things that are inside are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and he cuts the skin which is softened on the natural skin; then join the two lips with a suture, and if you see, stitch first the superfluity of the softened skin to three or four firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the  treatment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cauterization is common in our law, and for this reason I would like not to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the healers should know how to respond when asked about it, and know the cure; and the other, because we often need cauterization of some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and calves and other animals.  
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that a cautery is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, make the beast sit in hot water until the bones are softened and pliable; then grasp them with your hand until they are put back and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastisement of size: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut above each knot at the point, when you will have well scourged them; and leave no prick where the syfac and the subtle syfac are on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is more effective than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction perhaps nothing remains of the testicles, because the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.  
des hermofrodites	of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to II manners as men: one if it is that between the II sexes opens as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and it is upon the privy also like a rod and there are two openings. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure of man and woman is that you cut the attached cords, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine flows through the skin of the penis, there is no cure.  
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tumor is a lump attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you take the superfluity of the tissue to your hand or at the incision, and cut lightly; and do not cut too deeply, lest bleeding come forth, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed; and for one other sore that arises at the mouth of the wound, and the lip, and by chance falls out, and is according to the semblance of a cow, and for this they called it in old times "cow disease". 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cover it, as we have said the contagion, and the care until it is healed. 
de erratique	of wandering
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accident by illness that has come to it; or it is by a char fastened, or by the subtle or thick syfac, and it is made in the groin, or ribs, or below, or wherever; and prevents conception, and pregnancy, and perhaps flowers to have; and the knowledge of this one is by the examination of the bail.  
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppage is close to appearing, either to both or to one. 
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle syfac and it is near the two leaves, then haste, and do this: put your two index fingers together, and the woman be upon her back, legs spread; then make the two leaves form, until the subtle syfac is round, and be over the swelling; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and place it upon the place, and lie the woman down each day so that she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the knife is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you cut it with the spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh, then suspend it to the band and the cup; and take medicines that stanch blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and a bundle of egg white; then administer a wide poultice of wool, so that the wound may not close; and thus be long, and administer a tent of dry linen; then be cured with other dressings until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a boil comes in the marshes, it should be covered according to this manner, if it is not infected abscesses. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is in the marsh, one must not touch with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thulled; and we have said in the division the likenesses of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and boils, when they are opened in the flesh, and they do not appear to smell, except for the treatment by iron. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel, are those that one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It behooves you therefore to put the woman in a cold house, then is the altarul as tweezers, and the cope at its roots, then powder on restraining medicines such as acaice and dragon blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there comes bleeding, so let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confect it with honey and aisil, and make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stays in place, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If that is not the case, apply suction cups to the back and breasts without hurting; then take linen and moisten it in plantain juice or hawthorn juice with old wine, and apply it to the area. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, care for its place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is similar to the harsh chief, so it must be covered as I have said in the rule; and then the care until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come in the marshy areas, such as ulcers and boils and herpetic sores and tumors and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have said in the division.  
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary for me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marshes, which is not like abscesses that boil; and if you want to know the work of fire, look at whether the abscess is thick at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten yourself to pierce, but let him rest until the pain is quieted; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have him small seats so that he leans, and supports his back and assembles his feet toward the outside of the leg; and let his hips be spread out, and put his arms below his knees, and bind them well with a good bandage; then pull him gently toward the right side, and there administer the instrument by which one works on the mouth of the marrow, of this that comes after the form; and it is necessary that when you see administering this instrument, you put the tip first in to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters inside the instrument does not come deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he puts the cone of the instrument on top, and that he holds the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it soft with their hand, then it is necessary to cover at the top, at the spatula left; and when the wound is emptied, then it is necessary that you put into the wound tents moistened in rose oil, or in green dry oil; and place the tent from the wound to the edge of the margin, and place outside above the margin and on the lance clean cloth dipped in water or mallows be cooked; then cure after II days of ointment before this, until it is healed; and any time raise the margin and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and aristeloche long be cooked; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is put back in its place, it is necessary that you guard yourself from iron cautery, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The first thing to do is to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs of it when you see a woman press down and want to smell fresh air: then quickly the child feels the urge to come out; therefore, you know that this childbirth is according to nature, and the head comes out first, and the second follows; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press on her belly so that the child comes out soon; because when it comes out headfirst, the second follows, and the mother is rid of her superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes sometimes upon its feet, and comes further the body or shoulder, and the hands, or where it comes upon its belly, or groin, and is converted by chance upon its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary that the midwife be wise and subtle in these things, and avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should aid them.  
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes on its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth loudly, and the virtue of her is weak, then she make her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that is cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the small spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine, and cut at its fingernail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and hold the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman an enema of fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her sneeze and cough, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour: thus now the child will be born. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands are out, it is necessary that you put them gently back and forth; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up; then tip over the seat on the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when tipped over; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife which is before placed, and extract the child, and reset it equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on his feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon its feet, it is proper to push them upward; and then turn them back and forth, until they are even; then seize its feet and extend them back and forth. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	He jumps up to his hips if commanded to, and has it coughed out of condition; if he leaps further, God wills. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not healed as we have said, then return it little by little, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is gently set.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forward as we have said, then take muslinage of wheat and sesame oil and melted gum, and grind all in the mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in a hot bath until under the ribs; and when she is softened underneath, make her a collar of myrrh, and put it under, and let her stay for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and take her belly gently, because the child now jumps. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the exit of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands on and on; then let him be laid on his back, and have his legs hanging down, and lie on the bed; and he folds his hands on and on, and then he takes the hands on his belly, and removes the cushions below, until she is arranged down; and if the child does not jump, he takes his feet and moves them upwards, then moves the belly upward, then puts his hands; and he moves the child on and on; and commands the woman to keep pressing him as long as the child rises.  
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the exit of the child who comes out with a wide hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It behooves to engineer bringing back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on her bed, and uncross her legs; then administer the musculature that I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the stool, then try to bring back the hand; and when the child is born according to the natural figure, then make her sneeze, and command her that she should breastfeed until the child is weaned. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on his neck, and has spread his hands, and his face turned towards the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It behooves the bailiff to hold his hand, then turn it back and forth, and the other lightly; and when it is aligned, he puts on the muscle covering of the limb, as we have said, then he commands her to move back and forth; and when you have done this, make her sit in her seat, and command her to stretch; and she will sneeze.  
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to all the backbone
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner with the whole secondine, so cut the secondine at your finger, until the moisture is emptied; and if the infant can rise on its face and on its neck, then cut away from the bud, that it may not be held back, and let the infant die; then put the child inside, as long as you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to abstain at any time: then it will come out easily. 
de l’issue des gemelz	from the separation of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two things are strange and do not live, if they can be named; I know these, that they multiply, and are separated by the one who devises them, who is tied to the bud; and sometimes they come out as naturally as some others, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out violently, so the cure as we have said, and be the bandage subtle, and make quickly and lightly what she does; and make thus as it is worth to heal.  
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marshes I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of their glorious sage, and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all of them, because by chance something similar happens; so do according to what is necessary. 
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death; it is necessary that the woman be supported on her back, and her hips inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister the sheet from II parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not treated in the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the midwife with moist oils with musk of althea and fenugreek and flax seed, then oil the hands of the midwife with these oils and these muscillages; then put them into the womb lightly, then desire the place where she puts the pins that be suitable to those, and take ward if the child is appearing that it descends on its head; so put the pins in her eyes or in her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on feet, so put them or prickle and at the sides; and it is necessary that he hold the pin with his right hand, and put the curve between his two of the left hand, and put it to his whole hand lightly, and put the pin in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the pin:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then set against the other pin, or if you need it, the third one; so that the extractions are equal; and then move them equally on both sides, to move it easily, and let the pins be toothed to hold it well, as is shown in the form: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remains, he anoints the bail with some of his oil, and puts it in that part, and draws the other part; and if none remain, he places this on its own or higher place, and does so until it all goes out completely. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, then you should wrap it on the drape, until it is whole; then cut at the joint of the palm or at the wrist, and thus you should do to the other hand, and as II feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is stuck in the issue, or it has a sharp chief assembled, then it befits you to put the pointed spatula between your two, and make the chief and extract the sharp; or you take it to the instrument which is called "almidach," so that the form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way, do if the infant has a large chief naturally; and then pull out the bones with pliers, and if the head leaps forward and is strained by force, then it must be split, as long as the moisture which is or worse issue; and if it cannot issue, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then it befits that you pierce it until the moisture flows.  
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on his feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mouth of the wound is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is estrous in the belly or in the breast, then it behooves you to draw it out with the drape wrapped around the hand; and make the belly or the breast, as long as the moisture there is cured; and if the other members are taken away, and the head remains, then put the bail his hand in through the marrow; and draw it until the mouth of the marrow; then put the oncine or II, and draw it out; and if the mouth of the marrow is contracted because of a hot abscess that has come there, then it behooves not to work it, but it behoves to administer moist and fatty things; and administer plasters, and such in soft and moisting water. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on his side, and you can put him straight, follow what we have said about a living child; and if you cannot do so, then treat it by parts, and leave nothing of the secondary. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if it comes to the patients those that we have said in abscesses that come in the marsh; and if blood flows, let it be placed in water restraining, and give them other treatments. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been stillborn, then conceived another on top of it, and refused the other life.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, it came to her an abscess in her belly, and swelled so much that it opened, and began a great discharge.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long about it, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed greatly because this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and in my hands, I saw bones so that the woman was in a better place; and she lived for a long time like this, and it was coming back a little bit of bow from there; and I have not recorded this chapter further because for that reason, when the master finds a strange thing, he should know how to help.  
dou ramener la marris a son leu	how to bring the bone back into its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the clamp, as we have found in the books; and to two turns at two joints of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be large, and the edges of the trees it must, and long one palm and a half; and between the two limbs should be two adjustments of this same shaft, which are fastened on one and the other, of half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are put in the mouth of the handle to open when turning the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, to its semblance more subtle and lighter, be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the semblance of tongs; and have as II heads II adjustments, as you see, an arm's length long, and II wide; and when you see opening the mouth with all the instrument, so make sit the woman on the bed, the feet hanging and the legs open, then put the II adjustments adjusted together in the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips; then operate your hand to all the instrument, as you have done as tongs equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vagina, until the woman does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all surmounted, and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the eyes have appeared them, so much it is more hasty the work, and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you do not have appeared it, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her arm, and then make her sneeze with condiments, and hold her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she sneezes because of this, it is good.  
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If the mouth is not open, then take a pot and make it pierced or covered, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the abscess, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, boiled or pounded in water over the fire; then put one end of the chain or pierced pot and the other end in the mouth of the abscess, and hold it until vapors come out inside the abscess; then make it sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second part jumps hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure and is not worse, command the midwife that she moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in an ointment of althea, and then put it into the nature, and seeks the secondine; and when she will have found it, she takes hold of it and stretches it little by little straightly, so that the hairs do not fall out at the extraction; but it is necessary to move it lightly to right and left, and then pulls; if it comes and unties itself. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the marsh is closed and constricted, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, then guard that you do not apply to the milking; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marsh, that you tie it to the hip of the woman, then cleanse with ointment tetrafarmaçon; so it will become porous and return, and come forth; but nonetheless, when it becomes porous, evil odor comes to the stomach and head, and pales the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary then fumigations suitable to this: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument which one uses to fumigate the woman at childbirth retention is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen like a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide above the fire; and let the fumigation be upon the coals, and the tinder as long as it is burned, and begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	To examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but it is stopped by a subtle syfac: so it behooves the midwife that she pierce that syfac to its due, and she does not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guards the lacement that she does not touch it; then put on a fleece moistened in wine and oil, then the ointment cure until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, then put in the opening a piece of lead, and let him lay still for a day, and remove it when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this numbness comes from the closing of a wound or abscess; so it is necessary to cover that closure; if it is cured, as we have said about the cautery of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodules, and larger ones that come from near the foundation outside, or in the space of the two parts, if it is a fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works, and again moisture arises white or subtle bows, and sometimes these fistulas are pierced; and they are known by those who there is excretion or ventilation when the patient makes an excretion, and by adventure in jumping a few. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if fistulas that reach to the bladder and halfway up the penis; and extend to the groin joint, and to the buttock.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula piercing at the base, and not piercing; and it is that you put your right index or base, and put a subtle needle of iron or steel in the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has tortuosity, put in a tent of fine lead or horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair at your point; and if you do not feel it, and there is no coming out through emission or windiness or ver, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the urinary tract, then urine leaks out and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the hip, then the tendon comes to the place; if there is no twisting and the invention of the pain around, it is that it is a bow there, and there is no ointment medicine or bandage for it; and in these fistulas piercing there is no cure except labor, and vanity of the fools' wonders who meddle with them. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one who is not too young and not too old, there is hope of health by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly; then put a tent of lead, or of wood if there is tortuosity, as long as you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the base, you must put your index finger there, and then feel if the tendon is perceived; and be discovered or you feel between your finger the soft tissue or the bone, then you know that it is pierced; if you do not feel it, one cannot cure it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can by any means heal well some, but this happens rarely; and the help that one does, if one gently heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and puts it all hot into the fistula, until it comes near the foundation; and do this II times or III, as long as you know that these false hairs are burned, which resemble an eye feather; and then cure with damp cloths in butter, as long as those chars isse, then cure with ointment sealing and welding. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If so it is healthy, then well. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this [wound/condition] cannot be healed otherwise; and if it is caught between and does not pierce to the bottom which is the foundation, and between your bottom and the tent a thick covering of flesh or of silk, and you see the fistula following the covering of the heart; so you cut from the beginning of the fistula and push forward beyond the tent, and then use the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the top of the tent; and will be delivered the tent, and will fall; then defuse those fleeces that seem like an owl's feather, and nothing remains. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sans [meaning unclear] vaints, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together II good things: that is to say, the burning of these joined cartilages, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of damp tents in butter or in ground herbs, as long as the wound lies open, and if the cartilages are burned in the open; then cure the wound with soft dressings, bringing hard cartilage, and are the dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the bottom of the base, and is removed from the body, then you put on your own skin or foundation, and inquire about this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and there is the web or the syfac or chars, where it is close to piercing, if there is no other way except by hope and faith, by the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and care as first; and do not let too much be done, that you do not cut the tenement that holds the foundation, and comes the egestions by its own will; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that cover and the world after it is cut from its foundation, or by tent or by other appointed instrument; then cleanse the char fautree which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part outside the foundation: it will be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you place the tent in the fistula, and it is or lies against the base below the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:  
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts one twisted thread into two, and puts the tent to all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, as you put your finger or foundation; and pull the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to the other, and let it be for a day or two; and restrain it no time, until the threads join those that are between two, and stick together; then cure the wound until it is joined and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make a lance for the fistula if it is too deeply embedded, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spittle spinal bone from which one makes the fistula is very much one part and trenches; and on the other part no, because for that reason one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here. 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhages are according to II manners: or they are within the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, blood comes out, and there is one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture, and yet it is or a little bit of citrine water or a little blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation, is that you command the patient to stretch himself to go to chambers, until the foundations issue out, and appear the threads; so hasten, and it can be with pliers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots; and if the tweezers cannot hold it for its moistures, then take it with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois; and put them in your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle above some hot powders that be in their place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said or chapter of cautery, then cure the other cures until it is healed; and if the foundations cannot issue, then enema the patient with a sharp and pungent enema to wash out what is at the foundation, so that it can issue openly; since the patient is feeling better, and if the threads are outside the foundation, then the cure is light; and it is that you pick them up with your finger or with pliers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until it is healed, and that he fears the incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take I thread, and put it in a needle, and then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle, and so it be wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave I for the correction of the superfluity of blood; then put on the foundation I cloth moistened in rose oil or in cerote, and put on the foundation, and command to the patient that he rest; and then leave him until it dries, and when they will be dry, cure them with ointment and other cures, until it is healed.  
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying of the veins in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you scrape at the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above, which does not leave it to moisture; then treat it until it is healed as it should; and if it cannot heal, then begin the scraping more strongly than before, until it heals well, and be scraped; then treat it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	for trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formice is a small appearance made before the body, and goes much into it; and sometimes it finds it cold, and feels it also like dead fright, and comes throughout the body, and more to the hands than elsewhere. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane from an goose feather, or a vulture feather strong, and put that cane on the fremit, until the purple circles mark the fremit all around; then turn your hand on the whole cane until you cut all around the fremit, and put it in the middle, and scrape the fremit of its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this of a hound of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, but to keep at the two, and move pressing And if you see, so cauterize the groove, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No time is made clister of silver or brass, or iron melted or meshed; and no time is made of these instruments small and great, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those which one administers in the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is a severance where the belly is tied, as you see, and the shoulder is pierced inside; and on one of the sides II pierced, and on the other I; and the belly where one puts the medicines of a beast bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole I must have a space, then put into these holes I strong thread of thread spun crookedly in X or whichever way around, and assemble the belly like it is a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if one has the instrument before a strong thread, then enema; and this is the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or with egg yolk, or with something similar, then put it in gently; then squeeze the ministers with his two hands together, until it is all visible, then withdraw the clyster, and raise the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to go out, so let it flow as much as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him with the sickness of a falling belly, and the medicine hastens to issue, so restart it until it is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation or abscess, then the clyster be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin is restrained. 
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or we will tell you the cures of hands and of medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by blows of stone, and sword and knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; which are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or back, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head simple, because remembrance will come in its chapter.
