Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you guard yourself carefully that it is of a stone or similar things, and the skin is immediately torn and the wound is large, and you doubt heavily an abscess hot: so let the blood flow as soon as from the cephalic same even if it comes little blood from the wound, and be the bloodletting on the contrary side of the affected part; and avoid the patient's repletion of wine and coarse meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let his meat be reduced, and he drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no abscess hot, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if he has burned it, put on some ointment, until it is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together with tents, then bring them together with sutures, just as I shall say for wounds of the belly, by suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a point, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and cooked grain, also lentils, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a wound rotting and it doesn't reach the bone, then cut out all the rot and throw it away, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, then seize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put in this powder which binds as soon as the wound has closed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell; for do not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time should one make this with only quicklime when they lack incense or dragon's blood, but that the fire has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the herb has healed the wound, even if it is in a state, do not put this powder on it; but put some digested ointment, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it softens; then cure it with other cures until it is healthy. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then I will extract it with fine pincers; and I will tell you after this about the fractures of the head. 
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other means than to leave the cure, and put nothing restraining, because it harms the nerves and makes them retreat; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of this is with the brain, which is the highest member; but be the medicine warm, like calx washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucum laved also in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so stitch it and bind it with bandages, then care for it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is capped and full of bowe, then pierce or lower; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows, then cauterize, and stitch, and apply a bandage as the need is; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the keurs, and the duct is kept, by which the meat goes, then sew the heart on the cane of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural figure; and then restrain it well, and leave it for some days, then cure with ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then fix it; and if there are pieces of bone, then treat them all as much as you can, and what you cannot have, then let it rot as long as the wound festers, and be cleared and aligned the exit; and if the wound is fresh, then powder over it with the powder that I said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a lance blow or a knife wound, and the wound is deep, see if from the wound there are windiness as the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder in the first hour, nor bind it tightly so that the blood does not stagnate and return to the heart, and kill the sick person; but put attractive ointment in it, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton into the wound to draw out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound three days, or four, or more; so that there will not come any spasms, nor bad tremor of the heart nor constrictions of the breath; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Therefore, treat with tents and other dressings until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and work, then know that there is a fistula; so treat the wound as one must. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse, on the back, then the cure of those who are in front; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and it has broken pieces, then cure the wound, and remove the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, then let the wound rot, so that it will lighten the extractions; and for other wounds on other limbs is judgment as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is large and medium and small; from a great wound sometimes the intestine or nerves of the intestines come out because of which the introduction of others; and sewing is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse than a small wound because of which one puts the intestines back in more carefully, unless they put them back quickly into the heat; because that the intestine inflates as soon as they feel the cold, so they return more easily, and because of which the average wound is worse, because of which one must reset the intestine to its place than the others. And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners: the two common seams occur in the seam of the belly, and the seam of the other wounds of the body and two other special seams are common to other wounds; and nevertheless they are more common with the seam of the belly, and I will say one by one and declare.  
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines has emerged, and it seems to be better to put it back, then it is done in one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.  
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in hot water only, or you boil in hot water squinting and cypress and spike, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes do this binding, and move that only so as to deflate. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or wine and let it be cooked well, for by this is aligned the entrance to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument with which one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move that it be cut that no one should cut it without great need; and this is the instrument for cutting: so trench within in the curve and outside not, and see here the form. 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine has jumped out, put it back in according to its natural form in its proper place, if you are able, because it is good for healing. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, put his head and buttocks higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention to that the injured part be higher than the other; and thus you should administer what I say in great and medium wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Small wounds put what you have seen, then in your hands I minister pitiful that holds all the rupture with his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common manner of stitching, and it is that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave from the chief of the wound I doe of space, and there stick a needle where it has I good strong thread; and pierce the II heads of the skin with the II heads of the siphac, which is below the skin inside, until you make it pierced on that side, and assemble the II chief of the siphac the IIII together; then the strain of a double thread around the needle of II parts, then assemble the II heads of the wound conveniently, and then leave I doe of space, and there stick another needle; then lie the thread as you have done the first needle, and do not cease from this to do according to what you need needles, until the whole wound is constrained; and let the needles be medium, between subtle and thick, because the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot well enter: for this reason it behoves that they be medium; and it behoves not to put the needles too far out of the flesh and skin, k’they do not cut and open the wound before the sewing; and then cut the heads of the needles, so that they do not bleed the patient while sleeping, and I put tents or drapes on the heads of the needles for the mucus to keep, and leave them until the wound is sewn; and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because it suffices a needle or II Li second stitch is common, and it is that you assemble the II heads of the skin and the II heads of the syfac together on a needle where it has I medium strong thread; and when you have pierced these heads toz IIII together, then pull the needle back to the part where you began, in the manner c’on sews the drapes; and put space between each stitch the thickness of a minor doe; this stitch is evident to the man, and I sewed a wound with one hom had or belly, which was navred with a knife, and was the wound more than a palm wide, and it was intestines well II palms wide, and it was the wound in the middle of the belly.  
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been for twenty-four hours, and the wound was closed until fifteen days, and I treated it, and it was healed.  
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mire had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in the place where none were found, nor any medicines; and put half a sense more above the wound cotton twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the II proper manners of sewing: take the needle, and thrust it from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced the core straight through, lay the point down on the sheepskin or sew where you have put in the needle, and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the furrier does furs, and that you leave one part of the sheepskin one time, and take it back the other, until the sewing is completely done. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, as the Gauls say properly, is like any font, which assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one chief of the stitch to the other chief, in this manner: prick an needle or chief of the mirach prochiene, and make it pierce that place alone, and leave the two chiefs of the stitch; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part unto the inside, at the two chiefs of the stitch; then make it pierce one and the other from the outside part unto the inside, in two other chiefs of the mirach that are on the other side; and this is the middle manner of stitching and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galens says this word, and no one testifies to it, one must sew the belly with II needles, where there is thread in each; and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew ropes; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitch is more grievous than the others of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgements of the wound are such as the judgements of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh to all its blood, so long as the fire has cauterized it, then put back the intestine, and the wound; then put above the powder enchanting charcoal, and if the fire has cauterized it, then put above any ointment that be present, until the wound bows; and suck out the pus, and be soldered the skin, and the miracle; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then put upon it, as soon as it begins to bow, old cotton, and move it II times a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in several cases unless the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communion with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten the linen lightly in oil of tempered heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or rot in bowels, and many times happens, then give clisterize of black wine, and even if the rot comes to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called «jeun» cannot heal when it is ravaged, and that is because of the network of veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the probe jumps out of the wound, put it back as if the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned or black, then you should tie the part that is black, that bleeding may not come from there, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the tie, and put the two heads hanging from below the wound up to outside in order to align the extraction when the probe falls, and the wound bows. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, in some men it can be restored, because I saw that a man was wounded or belly of a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became infected and became a fistula, and there he excreted and flatulence; I put care according to what I could, and did not cease to treat until it was healed, and the edges fused.  
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I see him healed, I doubted that the patient had badly in his belly; and there was no harm, but stayed in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and they said any experimentors that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in this manner: take fremis to large testes, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the fremis has covered the mouth, so put it on the two lips, so that it strains its mouth up; and then cut the head, and this stays so that it cannot untie, then put the other fremit afterward in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely grasped; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief is burned in the intestine and causes no trouble to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is taken from the intestine of a beast, in this manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that is well stripped, and then tie it to the head of this fine thread of linen twisted, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and wind it in the rupture; and this way of sewing of frims is not more than according to the way of fiance and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the major intestines, there is nothing else but subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and even when it is closed and goes inward.  
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth knotted fault free and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also like the feather of a bird; and sometimes in clear bow, and other times thick; sometimes pock, and other times enough; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only because of one of the nine causes: it is to know, by the smallness of blood or flesh; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, that does not let flesh be born; or there is too much bow; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late healing, and inflated by nature; or there are veins or bones; and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is necessary that I make you know the cure of fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the syphysis, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so on that it comes to the property of the main member, and to the similar ones.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grief healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you want to know it, so take a tent of iron or tin, if the fistula is straight, so you will; and if the fistula is crooked, so make a circle with a subtle tent of lead, because the lead bends much around the crookedness; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it with tents, then cliserize it by one of the openings, because the moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleans it; then you will search carefully in your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and if it is covered deep, and ask well the patient about the pain that he feels at the pressing of your hand, and where he feels it; and when you will know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have said to you, then operate according to what I have said to you, and remove the filth and rotten things that are inside; and then care for it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep and straight, it is necessary that you cut as deep as you can, then put moist tents in medicine of vinegar, and put them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is deposited at the bottom; and then put a salves with healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by these, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, so cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then treat the king as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then cure the things in coming flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns as before, know that you are not well gone until the bottom: uncover and seek as long as you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore its place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.  
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too far along, that you cannot do anything about it; if there is nothing else to do but leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone that is corrupted, and you can draw it out with tweezers, if you extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, then you must draw them all out, leaving none behind; and if the moisture prevents you, and there is no error or fear, then cut through the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put on the wound a thing hindering rot, and leave until the flesh around the bones is rotten, then they will more easily loosen; and if it is large bones, like leg or thigh, then restor so long as the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of corruption, and comes up to the bone's marrow; you must be careful and cover all until the corruption, then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example from it and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so much that the substances came to the leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open; but the doctors by their folly opened it so much that the abscess opened, and they flowed out a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and many holes came which all emitted pus and moisture from the body; and many doctors treated him for about two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what flowed out through the holes a great deal; and the young man's body became red, and he had a yellow color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore attacked it, and dug into one of the openings until I discovered part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came to the inner bone; I removed what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but could not close it; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then tried to close the place; but I could no more than I dug into one palm of the bone, and it was broken throughout its length, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healed and closed quickly, and it did not need to begin again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of blood evacuation often but it was healed completely, and in the place of the bone a hard cartilage arose, and it was well disposed and had no inconvenience nor contrary in all things, neither to the going nor to coming. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it must be treated in this manner: take a linen cloth, and strain it to the head of the bone which opens, and command anyone that he extend it upwards; and put another linen cloth thicker than the first linen, and tie it on the flesh which is above the bone, and stretch the head so that you draw the corrupted flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh in the place where you see it should be, that the bone does not pierce the flesh; and put a splint or a board under the bone to move the corrupted flesh; and must stay as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and stay another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupt and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the whole flesh; then put the ember underneath, and then thread from one side to the other the corruption, and let the thread be as long as the length of the corruption; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and thread the bone where it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is nothing else to do than to cut; and if the corruption is in the heel of the hand or in the heel of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it opens for you; and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve do not oppose you; and know that the instruments to cut these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to equip yourself with each kind of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so therefore consider the instrument which you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder can be affected by internal or external causes; and when you have medicated that corrosion with the treatment of medicines, and they do not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the point where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes by this from death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the limb; and the signs are that the limbs become black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, then goes that corrosion of limb to limb, and takes over the whole body; so haste to cover it, and if it is from the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the arm, then cover it, and do not give it any space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, he cuts at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, he cuts the blade; and if it passes the blade, it is death, and there is no more treatment than the quantity of its virtue; and thus do all when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes in the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes on the foot, cut the whole foot; and if it goes up the leg, he cuts at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to leave the patient to die; and the way of cutting or sawing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister to the lower ligament, and another minister to the upper ligament, and you sever the flesh which is between the two ligaments at a spatula wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or saw, and put on each side a bandage of linen, so that the sawing does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient other lesion and abscess. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding comes when you operate, cauterize the place well, or you put some powders restraining on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the member injured with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and that corrosion first came in his sole of the foot, until it seized the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cover the foot, and it was healed; and long after that it returned the corrosion on the hand side, and it came to me, and I put on him things repelling after the cleansing of the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he begged me to cut off his hand, and I would not, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, that he would die, because the virtue of the man was weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his country, and hurried to cover his hand, and it was healed; and I have this tale told only for those who might need it. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	At no time comes an abscess in its fleshy place and stays so long that it makes a great assembly of bowels; and then they burst and pierce, and in jumping the bowel, and staying its vessels, as well as some vessels; and the skin which is above is also subtle as delicate drapery, and do not run up to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such disease is called "sain" and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it comes up to the bone even by force, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin so is that you cut that skin all around, and even when it is subtle, as well as some drapery; and does not heal for its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not yet complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, so treat it with a clyster thus: look whether the breast is large, and the bowel which is within it is of foul odor; then clysterize with Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take asafoetida, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and clysterize into the breast, and restrain the anus; and leave the medicine inside for II hours, then withdraw it by straining; do this many times, until the breast is purified, and the stench is removed; and sometimes clysterize with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of grapevine wood, and pour water over it, then filter it, and clysterize with it, until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the sick person cannot bear either the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then clysterize with water and honey in which there is a pinch of pounded litharge; or clysterize with honey and sweet wine, because the honey has the property of purifying and cleansing, and the wine makes it dry; and when you have done this, and you are convinced that the breast is well cleansed, then clysterize with what makes flesh grow in it, and it is that you take diaphana plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or clysterize with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken about the properties or treatment of ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, then enlarge it with iron a little, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basil ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up leaving only the space where the clyster can enter, and if the opening of the breast which stinks is above, then cut it or lower the place where it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bow is in place, let it not be hindered by flesh; and if you cannot cover the breast as well as you see fit, arrange it in such a manner that the bow goes to the lowest point it is at, for when the bow is in place, let it not be hindered by flesh, and if you cannot cover the breast as well as you see fit, arrange it so that the bow goes lightly down, and let nothing of the bow be left; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and stay on the linen cloth that covers the whole wound; then cut as strongly in the direction of the hole of the breast, a little wider than before; then put ointment beneath the other cloth according to the quantity of the wound, and put it on the wound of the breast to align the bow, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and the one that is on the hole of the breast, often remove to remove the bow, and know what comes out of the bow, if it is poison or pus or enough, or digested, or indigested; and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is in such a manner spread and you see the nature that jumps on the wound of the breast, know that the breasts are already healed, and approaching health; and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you open the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed indigestion after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after a long time, if it does not despair thee of health, for health approaches.  
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and those who do the opposite; and if he has an indigestible lump from the chest after many days, know that the breasts do not heal well; and if the breasts are slow to heal, and are swollen, then apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diafinit ointment, because there is a great part of vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; take diafinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the juice of old wine equal in substance; then confit it and use it; and the same thing is better cooked honey when the diafinit ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is over the fire; and then glue it to the breast, and put it on the breast; and sometimes administer a long aristolochia, and roots of celestial lily, which is also like flour of verbena and centaury; and use both simples and composites: grind them, and make powder, and put it on the honey that I said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not healed by this cure, then know that the corruption is deeper, and makes an impression in the bone, or in the hard limbs, or in the limbs; so the cure of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the ankle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or by chance in other two; and when it is neglected, and one does not take care of it, there comes I the abscess swells, and runs and digs a bow until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it corrodes the whole; and comes the corrosion up to the bone, so that there comes painful odor, and is the limb of the two wide, and is the color flux. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluity that is remaining from the angle, then cauterize the wound afterwards. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses against the flesh, and begins to prick, and the flesh bleeds, then it is necessary that you put oil under the nail so that it does not press on the flesh, and push it upwards, and cut that flesh skillfully and lightly, and put above the remaining flesh medicinal substances hot and corrosive to remove everything; then cure with ointments until it is healed.  
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then you cut it, and treat it well, for as long as the bone is corrupt, it cannot heal; and if you see the two [bones] corrode, then you cut it in I of us as it has been said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is broken, and beaten, and he feels great pain, then it is necessary that you first heal it; then cut the angle of the spatula sharp by cutting across above, and guard that the cutting does not come to the flesh which is under the bone, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, then put something on top which soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the hand's source
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and sometimes there is bone, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in some of us from the two.  
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any notch of the hip does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the hip, perhaps moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is light, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Whoever is born at the root of the joint, he is difficult to cure; so you must be careful when cutting it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must be at the back of the nut, it is fitting that you cut first the flesh around to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for this one, then cure it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The bandages that come to two together come by birth, or by soldering of a wound, or by burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you stitch together the suture, so that the parts repay according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or cloths softened in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or you put between two pieces of thin plank, until the joints are soldered, as it is fitting. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	The joining comes to none of his two with the palm, if he copes that joining as it is fitting.
des vils	of evils 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large vessels enveloped full of melancholic superfluities, that come in more members of the body; and more happen in legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, than to others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him once purging of colocynth, and then the healing of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is when you cut (it) and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein, and treat it completely. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The tail is done in this manner: first, raise the leg of hot water strongly, until the large vein is softened, then strain the leg of the sick person from above the hip to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in I place, or II or III, with a wide incision, then lift and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, as long as much blood comes out as the virtue of the sick person can suffer; and then bind it up, and command him to stay on meats avoiding black food; and begin the evacuation and the bleeding again when the veins are full, and harm the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the leg is done in this manner: lay the leg of the patient down if there is a lot of hair, then put it into a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it by fire, and then cut above the vein from the top of the knee to the bottom of the thigh, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with an incision, and scrape the vein on each side, until it feels apparent when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then put the point under, until it is lifted from the skin, and then press it onto the incision lightly, then cut it in another place three fingers above; then scrape the skin above the vein until it feels apparent, then lift it at the root, as you have done, and press it onto another incision, as you have done first; then cut another section, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut at the ankle, then treat and raise it up to the second section; then draw out in sections, until it is all drawn out, then cut; and if you cannot pull it and raise it, then put a needle through the thick double thread, and tie it and treat it, and put it under the point, and turn your hand on one side and the other, until it comes out; and guard that it does not break, for if it breaks, then one cannot pull or raise it, and it leads to nuisance to the patient; and when you have treated it all, put over the place of the wound wool soaked in wine and rose oil; and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to cut the vein is curved and does not cut, so it only cuts the vein; and is a large curve, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:  
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot places where no grass or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture; and by chance it may be found elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of rot that comes beneath the skin, as it comes from inside the body from snakes and worms, enmeshed between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then it changes its color, and the vein begins to come out as a root of a plant.  
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.
