When the bone of the shoulder is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of plank from one and a half to II inches, and tie it, and leave the plank on the leg, and all times that it has point to the fire, so wrap around the plank, and tie it; and if it is too long, so cut off a part, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it in its root, until it is entirely out; for if you cut it, it enters into the flesh, and brings abscesses and rot there, and bad illness; for that reason it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains on the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated from the palms of a length, or from X, and one hour came to me, who had it from X palms in length, and when you cut it, it puts I ray on the point, and pierce it to the bottom, so that all goes out; and be emptied the matter which is inside, and administer to the place medicines preventing rot any day, then cure it as the abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein the hands rain, and also when it opens in the joint of the foot, or where the foot is, and there comes much of piercing, and from which it jumps rains; cure therefore as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms which are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land “disease of the ox”, because it happens many times to oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well at the border of limb to limb, as long as they go through the skin where it goes, and jumps out; and is engendered by rot of some humors, as come worms and serpents and embers and ascarides in the belly; and doubt is had of its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it climbs to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see him cure and treat, one cannot force it except when it goes: so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong band tightly, then cut on top and pull the fur out, and if the root is too deep in the skin, and you don’t find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does, is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the eye, then hold below it the eyebrow firmly formed, then cut on top, and pull the fur out; and it is necessary to use the patient with cleansing of the body of medicines solutives for the humors of evil, and avoid meats that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything else, as if living silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later it spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it was returning towards the body, as I saw her. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed greatly how she moved so from limb to limb, because I have never seen this sickness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I have wanted many who had well moved pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and the veins uncovered, and because of this appeared that constraint windiness; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this malady, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then lie down above and below carefully, and then cut up until the constraint of wind is in its place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure with those who expel the winds, such as fetid pills, and seraphin pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that some have large points and small ones, and hairy, and smooth; and those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those where there are pieces; and the one which falls on any member, it falls in two ways: or on the principal member, such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.  
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you after, appear to you: then it is necessary that you abstain from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not yet completely embedded, then treat it, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and jumps the syvfac which is above the brain, it is when scotomia and sode and esvertin and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without fuer from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps loses speech and voice; and jumps from the wound moisture white seeming to poultice, and jumps also like burning of flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then hold yourself from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not inside. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were tied in a hard thing, not empty; and by chance the seventh moves as well as the hand, and in short black blood comes, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: know then without doubt that the death will descend. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the saette that never moves is that without plains of foam it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the ribs; and throws great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and moves all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perchance it leaps out of the wound something undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and leaps out no point of straw through the gut path, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine leaks out and comes outside, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs, and the similar members, are saved according to more dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that reason that you would do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that went into the root of his nose: I took it out, and pulled it from the other side under the fat of the ear, and it was cured without feeling anything. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And treated with an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye under the paper, and the arrow was removed, and could only touch the tip toward the shaft, and the arrow was large as a turquoise arc, all iron light without ears; the game was unharmed, and he did not suffer any bad accidents. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And treated an arrow in the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I removed the barbs, and carefully until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.  
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treated an arrow in a man, who it was in his chest or belly, and thought he would die; and then when he had passed XXX days, he did not change his disposition; I cut on the arrow, and removed it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.  
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who has an arrow that fell into his body or back and the wound was stitched up; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural positions, nor finds annoyance in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see I another man, to whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sewn together; and he remained so suffering great pain; and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow in the body of the prince the king, which was lodged between his ribs, and was a little tilted towards the right side; and the arrow was whole, and I was called to treat it after three days. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound was very tight. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt it as a whole thin tent, and I felt nothing at all; and he felt prickling and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put a poultice on top, astringent and digestive, for that reason the wounds didn't swell; and the wound from the arrow appeared.  
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the splint on his hand for several days, and sewed up the wound directly, and he stayed like that for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead one day inside his knee; and he told me so. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound medicine corrosive of water by hand for days, until it was open, and I tested it, and felt the head of the arrow that was hardening in its place; then I adjusted it in the opening of the wound with that medicine corrosive, until the head of the arrow appeared to me visibly; and it passed well the ends for IIII months, and then opened the wound so that I put tongs in it, and mine on one side and the other, and it could not go out; therefore I did not cease to subtly work and devise ways of instruments, until I took I day the tongs well made, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I treated it, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise men judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I therefore restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was healed completely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on those that I do not say, because the books cannot take everything; but the wise masters compare on very little thing, and on those that are present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, to the descent of foreign things that happen in this art.  
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are not in the limbs where they are lodged except according to two ways: either by their entry point or by another part; and that one which is lodged by the place where it enters, is an arrow entering into the flesh, and that is never the case now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, let it be left until the wound is entirely closed, and let it be moistened; and if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot come out, let it be left so for some days, and moisten it each day; and then when it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around it to all the forest fine, until the skin around is enlarged, and then treat it.  
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not draw it out, but let it stay until it is equal after a few days, because if the arrow comes to such a place, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not come up to the skin, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then the engine of the treatment. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply stuck and cannot be pulled out, then administer poultices as I told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned to its place in the body, and if one cannot see it, then search thoroughly throughout the entire tent; and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot by the tightening of the wound, and by the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or vein, then flay as much as the wound is large; and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears in the arrow to what it holds, then remove the flesh that is stuck on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can pull it out; and be careful that you do not break the arrow, so that you pull it out more roughly.  
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then bring it up until the joint is warm, then treat it, for the extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding goes against you, administer those that we have said in their chapter; and guard against the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put engine however you can move the arrow safely, soon or late, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow fell upon him, for this is the greatest aid that there be, and if you cannot do so, then put it according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where one does not see or feel anything of it, or the skin is swollen in the place so that if one sees or feels apparently: then cut there, as much as the pliers can take, and then extract it: if it jumps now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it for now, and then begin the extraction again until it is drawn out; and if the shaft is inside, push it with all your strength; and if the shaft has fallen, and you see to administer a thrust, administer the instrument as far as it goes so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then thrust, and if the arrow is stuck, push the instrument back in at its entry point, in order to facilitate the extraction.  
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is surrounded, it behooves you to cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then cure the wound as is fitting. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or in the belly or at the bladder or at the rib and it is close, and you can cover over it, if you should cover over it; and guard yourself from covering over the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then sew up the wound, if it is necessary; and take care of it until it heals.   
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to an eye beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the cutting head is like that of an bird's feather, for thrusting at the tip of the arrow, as here it is the form: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for inserting and holding is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one heals, of which there is XVI head, that is to say: II batans which are after the ears, which are called the two «herbech»; and the II arteries which are in the II temples appearing; and II veins that are in the II tear ducts of the II eyes, which are called «aspires»; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the chief of the neck; and the II veins which are in the neck; and the II veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins which are called «augeherich»; and II veins that are under the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly opened are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste," and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is on the fossa, and it is the one that is opened which opens manifestly above the elbow. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the sap vein is the one that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two veins; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one of them is below the curve of the pocket of the left side; and the second one called sophene which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called 'ness', which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of the bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then strap the patient's neck with a bandage, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their dependencies from the head: then put your hand, and where you feel the pulse below your hip, give it a slight blow; then take the lancet, and put it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein upwards, and cut through both the skin and the vein well two fingers wide, and make blood flow out as much as you see; then tie it up and keep it tied until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for old migraine, and sudden, and habitual ophthalmia, and to the body of the tears sharp to the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding are as I say: and it is that the patient restrain his neck, so long as the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your right hand, then sign in him; then raise the heart above the vein on your right index, and put the lancet below, and raise the vein up, and the cup, as you have done in the other veins, and make a cure of blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your right hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top; and then form the ligature, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about it and its treatment and its extraction, as begins the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the front forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein for ancient face ailments, and for migraine, and for blushing; and its qualities are that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fuser", whose form is here: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and hold with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never open it with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not right that the flames be too thick; and to heal across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the II veins that are in II tear ducts helps the eyes, and the ear, and the cheekbone, and to the canal in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the qualities of their blood is that the patient strains his neck by twisting with any linen, as before; then the vein, and whether the vein is through a point of length of flame a point wide, because there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, it may break; then make a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein from the nose is good for ague, and for sore throat, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his nose with your left hand, and takes a fine long thread, and puts it into the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too deep in the incision, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up at night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the thread:  
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the II  [a unit of measurement] helps in the treatment of the alaigne [possibly a type of bone or joint ailment], and at the beginning of meselerie [unclear medical term], and many diseases, and scabies, and corrosions, and herpes, and estiomenes; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient straitens his neck below one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then open the vein of the long one well, then draw the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then do the same to the other vein, then untie the linen, and constrain both veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until the morning, that the wound be healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the blood of the levers 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips from above helps to heal in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and to wounds and sores.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is to the right lip and the other to the left, and know them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins: therefore cut both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, so cut the largest of each side, and also do with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein under the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bloodletting of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the bloodletting of the cephalic, and it is to the stricture of the throat, and to the diseases of the eye, and to the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bleeding are that the patient lies between your hands before the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side a black vein: so bleed one and the other, and do not let them go too deep, because below are the arteries.  
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the cut from which one commonly heals are healed according to two manners: or they prick at all the flame martin wide, or olive subtle like cuts trenching, and is called "ane sil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame mirror is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is need to open the veins  with clear blood that is apparent and contains thick blood and troubled; and this is the form of the olive flame: 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for opening veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and neck, and chest, and belly; and it befits the healer that he drains skillfully, and that he keeps himself from the artery that is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it strikes the ground, and a flow of blood comes, then you must cauterize it, as I have said; and the flame should not be pricking but cutting like an anvil.  
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then you should constrain it, and change another; or you wish no vein of it, or you heal in its place the vein removing the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cut to the flame is healed, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you draw out the arm, that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse; then sign the place with a knife, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the inflamed flame; and guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflated, for it is from the artery: avoid therefore.  
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding upward like the urine of a child, and the vein is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: haste yourself then, and place your hand lengthwise upon it, then remove your hand if the vein is still throbbing; which many times happens. If the limb is swollen, and leave it so, and do not move it to the patient; and be in fear, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stained, and it weeps, and the medicine is not present, then cover the artery if it opens, for the head of the retraction; and stain the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a cork of pistachio, and make it, and take one of the halves and tie it on well until the other day; if it stays in place, that is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that staunch blood; and the stanching is not grieved in more dispositions for the small place of the wound, and the tightness of the linen of the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle helps so that it draws blood from the head above and from the body below, for this reason, it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and the surgeon must place himself in order to the nerve which is below, and if it is not too far apart, he finds the nerve, and he inflames it and the saints are pricked, and by chance, it cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in certain men because of its subtlety, then it is necessary that you feel the vein with the instrument again; and escape the nerve to your power. 
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then make a cut along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the head is so helpful that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed them with a pointed olive flame or a myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all veins, because it does not have tendons or nerves or arteries. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and do not grieve if it must be done the first time, and one begins again; and by chance swells the limbs in some men, when one tries it the first time, but it does not grieve.  
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The qualities of blood are according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting, is that bloodletting is administered only to preserve health and to ward off diseases to come; and let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins that are or cut: that is to say cephalic, femoral, and basilica; and one must bleed at the beginning of Lent on a Friday, and in autumn and winter after meals, when the sign of repletion appears; and one must bleed the first day or the third, after two hours or three days. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting that is administered for illnesses does not have a determined hour, but when need is of day or night, at all hours and in every time; and it is not proper to bleed children until XIV years, nor women carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not bleed the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some want to bleed, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that they cleanse the intestines with a light enema, if they have much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not draw in the superfluous impurities harmful to the principal members; nor should one bleed who is too fattened with meats, nor who is drunk, as long as he is so, nor those who are dropsy; and if it happens after colic, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and multiplication of labor in woman, and childbirth, and vigil, and fasting, and any of those things that total virtue, or by thing of the arm or of the body; then subtilize the humors, if his blood is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the skill for it; then enter into a bath, if nothing forbids it, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein of the arm near the elbow, as we have said; and keep yourself free on that day from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be lying and joyful, and let the one who bleeds be higher than him who bleeds, and rub the arm two or three times, then pull back the bandage halfway, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell, and you feel them; then moisten the bleeding point with a drop of old oil, then put his finger of his left hand on that vein below the elbow about an inch where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not move and fail during the incision. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that are like cords to the vein-drawer, and some that are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if it opens the vein, the wound is too tight, for this reason it is necessary that the vein-drawers be aware of these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, it is restarted once more a little below where it was or above carefully, if the area isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient fears it, let him leave it for one or two days, and bind his arm not: perhaps there will come boils in its place; nor enter into water baths, then re-begin the bleeding if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or the vein is too fine and you doubt that there is as much blood as you see, pierce again in that same wound straight to the entire flame; and work one point gently, so that the limb is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place inflamed, do not start the bloodletting again, and put on a bit of oil, because it will calm the body of blood, and is mixed in this place with the oil; and thus administer the oil to each wound that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing heals triacle and borage, when one puts it on the place; so subtly does it reduce swelling and separate it when it is too big. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes an abscess, which happens often, even when it is not drained except for the time that the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the place a sponge moistened in water and some hot oil, and restrain it for one hour; and you must do this after the blood has come out of the vein, and if it remains in place after several days without any blackness or greenness, then it does not harm him; and if you see it, put on any thing of aloes or frankincense mixed with juice of calamine, mustard, or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance at the saint's basilica happen: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft at the compression of the hand, then is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, I advise you that you do not put upon it anything of what we have said, because perhaps a vein lies within; but make one dry plaster to harden the place, then cure with another cure, until it be healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it drain until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it shrink until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for him who is fat and full, and needs the extraction of blood, one makes a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed little and often, and one must bleed by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from the decrease of blood and the cutting of nerves, and is worth more than the bleeding through long or wide. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose body is weak from bloodletting, it is fitting to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is feverish, treat him with blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, put softened bread before the bloodletting in quince syrup, or in honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it bleeds at the vein, after the evacuation of much blood, then it is necessary that he moisten broth of flesh and fragrant syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the opening of veins. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to drain his arm, and bleed other times if necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he should bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to drain his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another place, he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body that has already become hot and causes fever; so it is necessary to milk a large quantity, and widen the opening as much as it falls into pieces of bread; then that you reward all the conditions of health, and put your hand on his arm while he heals, that death does not come in the place of pieces of bread, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it does not suit when you see to untie the arm, and make blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly; nor if it is curved, that he extends his arm too much, for that would be bad; but let him rest as long as he heals the second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, as long as the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein flows out, and put on top of a piece of gauze back in shape, and press lightly.  
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, leave it and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to draw blood for the second time, let it heal in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein from which blood is drawn from the arm is located near the vein of the neck because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein is that the patient plunges their hand into hot water until the bone is red; then it should be tied moderately so that the vein appears well, then it is lanced through, not too wide nor too long; and let the opening be large, and lance well near the joint of the hand, and if one cannot withdraw blood, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood to collect in the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back into hot water, because it is put in more in winter than in summer; and the lancing of this vein is safer of all other veins, because there are neither arteries nor nerves. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The vein of the savior of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and put it in hot water, as long as the vein is swollen, if one sees it; and if the vein is crooked, and if you cut it completely, it does no harm; and do not go too deep in the puncture, for the nerves are below all covered with skin, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot exit. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and wool on top of the vein to close it well, and do this with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of the left hand is good for the disease of mice, and do everything as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophorene is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and hips and old legs, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salve are that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs upon the vein until it perspires, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many rains; heal therefore whether larger rain, or at the ankle, which is more valuable. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you drain it on the foot, guard the nerves which are below, and drain it by traversing as when cutting; and let the flames be anethesing.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot draw out blood from it, put the foot in water, and let the vein be emptied well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the sutures are required for the first time, redo them a second time above by a little, because the skin is salty; and do not doubt of the nerve, as we have said, and so do the same with the splint from the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of fury, and its incision is worth for the pain of the hip when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of his vein are such that the patient enters into a bath and is restrained above the ankle four times by twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, you cleanse the vein in all ways that you can, and across; and it is better that you cut it than that you let it remain dry, because the place is dry, and she is much filled with a lot of blood. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, search for any vein that opens or back of the foot, and toward the small thigh, and guard the nerves; and make as much correction of blood as you see, and then untie the band, and put on cotton and restrain it; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of  suction cups healths 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Windsucks are made of horns, or glass, or wood; and suction is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is to be done with fire is according to II manners: or it is all fire, or without fire; and cupping which is done by striking and by extraction of blood, is done in XIIII places of the body, so that one is all in the head; and the other is in the neck; and II others in II ribs of the neck; and the cupping below the chin; and the cupping on the II shoulders; and the cupping on the hips; and the cuppings between the II arms; and the cuppings on the II legs; and the cuppings on the II ankles; and cupping does not treat of blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken anyone, as one does with bleeding from a vein; and it is not necessary that it should be administered, neither all fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all of the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to bloodlett, or for customs, let us bring them each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every time; for there are some who when they have need to bloodlett, have heavy head; and there are those who feel fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and bleed; and there are some who dream, and see by blood and wounds and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is emitted during the month, we command to vomit after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the muse helps the heat of the head … that comes to the eyes, and it is not proper that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosation is in place of the bloodletting of the cephalic, and it is not proper that those who are of cold complexion use it, or who have a cataract, because it does much harm to them; and for this reason, it is not proper that the elderly use it, nor those who have or heads cold diseases. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are healed by it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to put the suction cup a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The windpipe brings the neck to the place of the vein of the head and of the basilica, and because of this it is good for the treatment of the lung, and for cutting the channel of the heart, and all, and for inflation; and it is necessary to put a little bit in, because if it holds too tightly, it causes obstruction in the stomach or heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation of the II ribs of the neck is good for headaches and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the vein of the basilica; and you must command the patient to stretch his hand when putting it on, so that he does not cut the artery, and there will be no running of blood. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosation below the chin is worth against diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for diseases that come from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The bleeding of the veins is as valuable as that of three veins in the arm because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to have them pierced too deeply, because the vein is bare of flesh, and close to nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids from the foundation, and for diseases of the bowels, and it should be large and of iron so that it needs to well suck; and by chance if it were thin, it would break; and there will make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses of the legs are sucked open well, because they attract blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the thighs, and of the bladder, and soften the joints; and they are placed in the place of the two shins, and of the two ankles, but all the same they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of placing the cupping glass is that you put it first empty, and suck moderately, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease from this doing until you see the skin red and inflamed, and appear the flow of blood; then fix, and replace the cupping glasses, and take heed to the disposition of the body, because there are those who have thick flesh, and porous skin: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a poke deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to prick it two times; the first time to make a subtle way for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only make one incision.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.
